Foundation to extend the lease for an additional year commencing on April 1, 2026 through March 31, 2027; and
authorize its execution by the City Librarian.

5.
AB 481 Annual Military Equipment Report — Approval
Approve the Annual Military Equipment Report per California State Assembly Bill No. 481.
CEQA: This action is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is an organizational or administrative activity that
will not result in direct or indirect physical changes in the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)(5).)
6.
Real Time Information Center — Agreement
Approve a license agreement with Franklin Templeton Companies, LLC, for occupancy of office space located at 1
Franklin Parkway in San Mateo, to support the expansion and continued operations of the Police Department
Real Time Information Center in the amount of $1/month; and authorize the Chief of Police to execute the
agreement in substantially the form presented.
CEQA: This City Council action is exempt from CEQA review under the “common sense” exemption, because it can
be seen with certainty that there is no possibility that the proposed license agreement may have a significant
effect on the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15061(b)(3).)
7.
City of Foster City Interest on Wastewater Treatment Plan Payments — Agreement
Approve an agreement with the City of Foster City to receive an interest payment for the Wastewater Treatment
Plant Master Plan Improvement Projects in the amount of $148,141.70; and authorize the City Manager to
execute the agreement in substantially the form presented.
CEQA: This agreement is not a project subject to CEQA, because it consists of a government fiscal activity which
does not involve any commitment to any specific project which may result in a potentially significant physical
impact on the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)(4).)
8.
Citywide Capital Project Appropriation Amendments — Adoption
Adopt two Resolutions to adjust appropriations for certain Citywide Capital Improvement Program projects.
CEQA: This Resolution to adjust appropriations for certain capital improvement projects is not a project subject to
CEQA, because it consists of a government fiscal activity that does not involve any commitment to any specific
project which may result in a potentially significant physical impact on the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section
15378(b)(4).) Each individual project described in this Agenda Report and Proposed Resolution has/will be
individually reviewed under CEQA.
9.
Microsoft Enterprise Agreement Subscription Increase — Approval
Approve a subscription increase to the City’s Enterprise Agreement (EA) with Microsoft for Office software,
Windows desktop operating systems, and server products for Year 3 of the existing three-year agreement in the
amount of $28,604.24, for a new total of $794,341.24; and authorize the Director of Information Technology to
execute the subscription increase in substantially the form presented.
CEQA: This subscription fee is not a project subject to CEQA, because it can be seen with certainty that it will not
cause a physical change in the environment. (Public Resources Code Section 21065.)
10.
Customer Relationship Management Software and Services — Amendment

12.
Temporary Sign Placement Enforcement Policy During Election Periods — Adoption
Adopt a Resolution to approve the Temporary Sign Placement Enforcement During Elections Policy to standardize
guidelines for the City's enforcement of temporary signs in accordance with San Mateo Municipal Code Title 25

CEQA: This policy is not a project subject to CEQA, because it can be seen with certainty that it will not cause a
physical change in the environment. (Public Resources Code Section 21065.)
13.
Operation of Leaf Blowers — Ordinance Adoption
Adopt an Ordinance to amend San Mateo Municipal Code Chapter 10.80 "Operation of Leaf Blowers" to prohibit
the use of gas leaf blowers.
CEQA: This Ordinance Adoption is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is an organizational or administrative
activity that will not result in direct or indirect physical changes in the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section
15378(b)(5).)
14.
Reach Codes for the 2025 Code Cycle — Ordinance Adoption
Adopt an Ordinance to amend San Mateo Municipal Code Chapter 23.24 "Energy Code" to require energy
conservation measures for air conditioner alterations, replacements and installations in single family homes,
duplexes and townhomes; energy conservation measures for heating, ventilation and air conditioner
replacements and installations in nonresidential buildings; and increased efficiency and electric readiness
requirements for additions and alterations to single family homes, duplexes, and townhomes.
CEQA: This Ordinance Adoption is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is an organizational or administrative
activity that will not result in direct or indirect physical changes in the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section
15378(b)(5).)
15.
Citywide Fire, Life, and Safety Inspection Testing and Maintenance Services — Revised Agreement
Adopt a Resolution to use an alternative purchasing method to award a five-year agreement with APi National
Service Group, Inc. for inspection, testing, and maintenance of Citywide fire, life, and safety systems in the
3 of 424

--- page 4 ---
amount of $591,357; approve a contingency reserve of $60,000; and authorize the Public Works Director to
execute the revised agreement in substantially the form presented and issue change orders within the
contingency amount.
CEQA: Approval of an agreement for inspection, testing, and maintenance of Citywide fire, life, and safety systems
is categorically exempt from CEQA as an “existing facility,” because it consists of the operation, repair,
maintenance, permitting, leasing, licensing, or minor alteration of existing public or private structures, facilities,
mechanical equipment, or topographical features, involving negligible or no expansion of use. (CEQA Guidelines
Section 15301.)
16.
Citywide Street Reconstruction Phase 5 — Agreement
Approve an agreement with Teichert Construction in the amount of $4,274,912; establish a contingency reserve
in the amount of $855,000; and authorize the Public Works Director to execute the agreement in substantially
the form presented and issue change orders as allowed by the contract documents and within the contingency
amount.
CEQA: This project is categorically exempt from CEQA as an “existing facility,” because it consists of the operation,
repair, maintenance, permitting, leasing, licensing, or minor alteration of existing public or private structures,
facilities, mechanical equipment, or topographical features, involving negligible or no expansion of existing or
former use. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15301.)

amendments within the contingency amount.
CEQA: Approval of this amendment is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is an organizational or
administrative activity that will not result in direct or indirect physical changes in the environment. (CEQA
Guidelines Section 15378(b)(5).)

Adopt a Resolution to authorize the City Manager to execute and submit an allocation request as required by the

21.
Marina Lagoon Spot Dredging Project, Bid Rejection — Approval
Adopt a Resolution to reject all bids received for the Marina Lagoon Spot Dredging Project.
CEQA: This Project will be performed pursuant to the terms and conditions of an existing permit with the
environmental regulatory agencies for the Marina Lagoon including the San Francisco Bay Regional Water Quality
Control Board. On July 7, 2021, the City filed a Notice of Exemption with the Office of Planning and Research and
the County Clerk-Recorder for the County of San Mateo (SCH No. 2021070131) for proposed maintenance
activities for the Marina Lagoon, effective from 2022 through 2026. These maintenance activities are
categorically exempt as existing facilities as they involve negligible or no expansion of existing or former use.
(CEQA Guidelines Section 15301.)
PUBLIC COMMENT
Members of the public wishing to comment on any item not appearing on the agenda may address the City Council at this time. State
law prevents Council from taking action on any matter not on the agenda; your comments may be referred to staff for follow up.
Public comment is limited to a total of 15 minutes; however, an opportunity for additional public comment may be provided later in
the agenda.
 
PUBLIC HEARING
City Council action on the following public hearing(s) represents a final decision concluding all administrative proceedings. Judicial
review may be had only if a petition is filed with the Court not later than the 90th day following the date the decision is made.
Judicial review of environmental determinations may be subject to a time period for litigation as short as 30 days following the date
the decision is made.
 
22.

2026.
CEQA: This action by the City in setting the maximum rates to be charged by Recology San Mateo County relates
to funding an on-going solid waste collection service and is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is a
government fiscal activity which does not involve any commitment to any specific project which may result in a
potentially significant physical impact on the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)(4).)

ADJOURNMENT
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
AGENDAS: Agendas and material are posted on the City’s website on the Friday preceding each Council Meeting and can be viewed on the City's
website at www.cityofsanmateo.org . Any supplemental material distributed to the Council after the posting of the agenda will be made part of the
official record.
WATCHING A MEETING ON TV: City Council meetings are broadcast live on Comcast/channel 27, Wave/channel 26, or AT&T/channel 99.
For transmission problems during the broadcast, please call (650) 522-7099. For all other broadcast comments, call (650) 522-7040, Monday-Friday,
8 a.m. - 5 p.m.
WATCHING A MEETING ON A COMPUTER: There are three ways to stream.
1) Public Meeting Portal www.cityofsanmateo.org/publicmeetings
2) City YouTube channel and stream it on YouTube: http://youtube.com/CityofSanMateo
3) Watch TV live stream: https://www.cityofsanmateo.org/193/Channel-San-Mateo-Live-Stream 
PUBLIC COMMENTS/REQUEST TO SPEAK
Prior to the Meeting 
Send comments to: clerk@cityofsanmateo.org until 4 p.m. the day of the meeting.
During the meeting
By Zoom: Click the link at the top of the agenda and you’ll be added to the meeting. All attendees are muted by default. When the item of interest
is open for consideration, select the “Raise Your Hand” icon and you will be called on at the appropriate time.
By telephone: Call (408) 638-0968 and enter the conference ID found at the top of the meeting agenda. When the item of interest is open for
consideration, select *9 to raise your hand. When called upon, press *6 to unmute, state your name and provide your comments.
In Person: At the meeting complete a “Request to Speak” form, submit a request at the speaker kiosk or scan the QR code.
ACCESSIBILITY: In compliance with the Americans with Disabilities Act, those with disabilities requiring special accommodations to participate in
this meeting may contact the City Clerk’s Office at (650) 522-7040 or clerk@cityofsanmateo.org . Notification 48 hours prior to the meeting will
enable the City to make reasonable arrangements to ensure accessibility to this meeting.

SUBJECT:
San Mateo Public Library Foundation Operating Lease — Amendment
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve an amendment to the Property Lease and Operating Agreement with the San Mateo Public Library Foundation to 
extend the lease for an additional year commencing on April 1, 2026, through March 31, 2027; and authorize the City 
Librarian to execute the revised agreement in substantially the form presented.
BACKGROUND:
The San Mateo Public Library Foundation (SMPLF) leases office space in the Main Library to accommodate Foundation 
employees who perform fund development duties in support of the Library Foundation's mission. The Commercial 
Property Lease Agreement and Operating Agreement between the City of San Mateo and San Mateo Public Library 
Foundation was signed on December 14, 2007. Subsequent lease extensions through March 31, 2026 have been approved 
by the City Council. This Amendment represents a one-year extension of the lease agreement from April 1, 2026 through 
March 31, 2027. In FY 2025-26, the Library Foundation awarded $175,000 for support of programs and collections. The 
successful 2024 and 2025 fundraising events made it possible for the Library to offer an enriching Summer Learning 
Challenge Program, enhance the general collection, and provide cultural and educational events through four cultural 
committees. 
BUDGET IMPACT:
In consideration of the financial support the SMPLF fulfils on behalf of the San Mateo Public Library, the rental amount of 
the lease will continue to be set at the nominal rate of $12 per annum.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This lease agreement is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is a government fiscal activity which does not involve any 
commitment to any specific project which may result in a potentially significant physical impact on the environment. 
(CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)(4).)
NOTICE PROVIDED
All meeting noticing requirements were met.
ATTACHMENTS
Att 1 – Lease Agreement.

SUBJECT:
AB 481 Annual Military Equipment Report — Approval
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve the Annual Military Equipment Report per California State Assembly Bill No. 481.
BACKGROUND:
On September 30, 2021, Assembly Bill 481 (AB 481) was codified in Government Code Sections 7070-7075, requiring the 
governing body of law enforcement agencies to adopt a “Military Equipment Use” policy. The San Mateo Police 
Department presented a policy to the City Council which was adopted by Ordinance on May 2, 2022. 
AB 481 also requires law enforcement agencies to prepare an annual report containing information for the preceding 
calendar year. Staff has prepared a Military Equipment Annual Report (Exhibit A) which summarizes the required 
information, including a description of the purpose of the equipment and how it was used; any complaints received; the 
results of any internal audits; the cost of the equipment; the quantity possessed; and if the agency intends to acquire 
additional equipment in the next year. 
The San Mateo Police Department does not possess any tactical equipment obtained from the military, nor does it possess 
any equipment designed for military use. The term “military equipment,” as defined in AB 481, includes various items 
commonly used by law enforcement agencies as part of best practices to reduce risks to community members. The list 
includes, but is not limited to, unmanned aerial or ground vehicles, armored vehicles, command and control vehicles, 
chemical agents, less-lethal shotguns, less-lethal 40mm projectile launchers, distraction devices and long-range acoustic 
devices. These items provide peace officers the ability to safely resolve volatile situations and are vital tools that facilitate 
compliance with our stringent use of force policy. These tools have been tested in the field and are used to enhance citizen 
and officer safety. 
During the 2025 calendar year, no formal complaints related to military equipment were filed with the Police Department. 
There were no violations of department policy related to the deployment of military equipment by department personnel. 
No new items of military equipment were acquired in 2025. In the current 2026 calendar year, the Police Department 
plans to retire three (3) unmanned aerial system (UAS) devices, and acquire four (4) new devices, to support activities of 
the Real Time Information Center.  
In compliance with AB 481, the Military Equipment Annual Report was published on the Police Department’s website at 
least 30 days prior to this meeting.

San Mateo CA 94403
www.cityofsanmateo.org
Agenda Number:  6
Section Name: CONSENT CALENDAR
Account Number: 10-5112
File ID: 26-10955
TO:
City Council
FROM:
Alex Khojikian, City Manager
PREPARED BY:
Police Department
MEETING DATE:
March 16, 2026 
SUBJECT:
Use of Office Space for Real Time Information Center — Agreement 
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve a license agreement with Franklin Templeton Companies, LLC, for occupancy of office space located at 1 Franklin 
Parkway in San Mateo, to support the expansion and continued operations of the Police Department Real Time 
Information Center in the amount of $1/month; and authorize the Chief of Police to execute the agreement in 
substantially the form presented.
BACKGROUND:
The Police Department has been steadily growing the operation of the Real Time Information Center (RTIC) over the past 
year.  This significant investment in technology is actively transforming the way we serve the community and support field 
personnel.  The RTIC provides for enhanced situational awareness, strengthens interdepartmental coordination, and 
improves response capabilities through real time monitoring and information sharing.  
Since its inception, the RTIC has experienced significant growth in both operational scope and staffing. The existing 
workspace is no longer sufficient to accommodate the technology infrastructure, personnel, and equipment necessary to 
sustain and expand RTIC functions.  As a result, staff have explored options for additional office space within close 
proximity to existing public safety operations.  The global headquarters for Franklin Templeton Companies is located 
adjacent to Police Department.  Franklin Templeton has a strong track record of supporting the City’s public safety 
objectives and community partnership efforts, and has offered the City use of vacant office space located at 1 Franklin 
Parkway, for a nominal cost of $1/month.  The license agreement is on a month-to-month term, and may be terminated by 
either party with 30 days notice. The proposed space is within close proximity to current operations, minimizing disruption 
and maintaining operational efficiency.  The license agreement will provide adequate square footage to accommodate 
current RTIC staff and equipment as well as anticipated growth; space for installation of desks, computer monitors, radio 
equipment and collaborative work areas; immediate availability; and a rate that represents a substantial cost savings. 
The Police Department has been designated to receive funding in the amount of $550,000 from the United States 
Department of Justice Office of Community Oriented Policing Services FY2026 Technology and Equipment Program (TEP), 
and anticipates receiving these funds later this year.  Staff intends to use these funds to outfit the RTIC space with desk 
workstations, computers, and any necessary radio and technology equipment.  No General Fund appropriation is 
requested for furniture or equipment associated with the RTIC expansion.
BUDGET IMPACT:
The cost of the license can be accommodated within the Police Department’s current adopted budget appropriation.

CITY OF SAN MATEO
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This City Council action is exempt from CEQA review under the “common sense” exemption, because it can be seen with 
certainty that there is no possibility that the proposed license agreement may have a significant effect on the 
environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15061(b)(3).)  
NOTICE PROVIDED
All meeting noticing requirements were met.

LICENSE AGREEMENT FOR OCCUPANCY OF PORTION OF 
ONE FRANKLIN PARKWAY, BUILDING NO. 960/1 
SAN MATEO, CA 94403 
 
THIS LICENSE AGREEMENT (the “License") is entered into by and between Franklin Templeton 
Companies, LLC, a Delaware limited liability company with a place of business at One Franklin 
Parkway, San Mateo, CA 94403  (“Licensor”) and City of San Mateo a governmental entity with a place 
of business at 200 Franklin Parkway, San Mateo, CA 94403   (“Licensee”), effective as of the signature date 
hereof. 
 
WITNESSETH: 
 
WHEREAS Licensor and Licensee desire to enter into this License to govern Licensee’s use of the 
Licensed Space subject to the following definitions. 
 
The “Building” is the building located at One Franklin Parkway, Building No. 960/1, San Mateo, CA 
94403. 
 
The “Furniture” the office and workstation furniture, including office tables and chairs, conference 
tables and chairs, couches, coffee tables, video cameras and TV monitors located within the Licensed 
Space as of the date hereof.   
 
The “Licensed Space” is located in the approximately six hundred forty nine (649) rentable square feet 
on the first floor of Building 960 (the “Building”) as shown on Exhibit A attached hereto and made a 
part hereof.   
 
The “Common Areas” shall mean restrooms, lobbies, stairwells, break room, coffee room and 
conference rooms located on the first (1st) floor of the Building, and non-reserved surface parking spaces 
and the parking garage under the Building. 
 
“Hazardous Materials” shall mean any “hazardous or toxic materials (as such materials may be 
identified in any federal, state or local law or regulation), provided that the foregoing shall not be deemed 
to proscribe the use by Licensee of customary office supplies in normal quantities so long as such use 
comports with all applicable laws.”

The grills, louvers, skylights, windows and doors that reflect or admit light and/or air 
into the Licensed Space shall not be covered or obstructed by Licensee, nor shall any articles be placed 
on the window sills, radiators or convectors. 
4. 
Licensor shall have the right to prohibit any advertising by any tenant or licensee which, 
in Licensor's opinion, tends to impair the reputation of the Building, and upon written notice from 
Licensor, Licensee shall refrain from or discontinue such advertising. 
5. 
Common areas within the Project, including, without limitation, the Common Areas, 
shall not be obstructed or encumbered by Licensee or used for any purposes other than ingress of egress 
to and from the Licensed Space and for delivery of merchandise and equipment in a prompt and efficient 
manner, using elevators and passageways designated for such delivery by Licensor. 
6. 
All locks or bolts of any kind shall be operable by keys provided to Licensor.  Licensee 
shall, upon the termination of its License, deliver to Licensor all keys of stores, offices and lavatories, 
either furnished to or otherwise procured by Licensor and in the event of the loss of any keys furnished 
by Licensor, Licensee shall pay to Licensor the reasonable cost thereof. 
7. 
Licensee shall keep the entrance door to the Licensed Space closed at all times. 
8. 
All movement in or out of any freight, furniture, boxes, crates or any other large object 
or matter of any description must take place during such times and in such elevators as Licensor may 
reasonably prescribe.  Licensor reserves the right to inspect all articles to be brought into the Building 
and to exclude from the Building all articles which violate any of these Rules and Regulations or the 
License.  Licensor may require that any person leaving the public areas of the Building with any article 
to submit a pass, signed by an authorized person, listing each article being removed, but the 
establishment and enforcement of such requirement shall not impose any responsibility on Licensor for 
the protection of any Licensee against the removal of property from the Licensed Space. 
9. 
All hand trucks shall be equipped with rubber tires, side guards and such other safeguards 
as Licensor may require. 
10. 
Licensee shall not have access to the Building's roof, mechanical, electrical or telephone 
rooms without permission from Licensor.

SUBJECT:
City of Foster City Interest on Wastewater Treatment Plan Payments — Agreement
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve an agreement with the City of Foster City to receive an interest payment for the Wastewater Treatment Plant 
Master Plan Improvement Projects in the amount of $148,141.70; and authorize the City Manager to execute the 
agreement in substantially the form presented.
BACKGROUND:
As part of the Clean Water Program, the Wastewater Treatment Plant Master Plan Improvements Project (Project) 
expands and upgrades the existing San Mateo Wastewater Treatment Plant. City staff manages the Project and its 
finances. 
Beginning in April 2023, San Mateo advanced Foster City’s share of project costs due to debt-related cash flow constraints. 
As a result, San Mateo lost interest earnings it would otherwise have earned, while Foster City retained and earned 
interest on its cash. Due to staff turnover in San Mateo, no written agreement governing these advances was executed, 
nor was Foster City invoiced for its share of Project costs. 
The cities now agree that Foster City shall reimburse San Mateo for foregone interest earnings for the period of April 2023 
through November 2023, when Foster City requested an invoice to pay its full share of the cost. The proposed agreement 
is included as Attachment 1. Details of the reimbursement are as follows: 
• Interest is calculated at 1.9%, equal to the Clean Water Program’s average debt cost. 
• Interest is applied to the monthly advances which accumulated to $19,665,305 in November of 2023. 
• Total reimbursement amount equals $148,141.70 (as shown on the invoice in Attachment 2).
Based on the above, staff recommends Council to approve the proposed agreement to receive an interest payment from 
Foster City in the amount of $148,141.70.
BUDGET IMPACT:
There is no budget impact from this agreement. The interest revenue was anticipated to be received in this fiscal year.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This agreement is not a project subject to CEQA, because it consists of a government fiscal activity which does not involve 
any commitment to any specific project which may result in a potentially significant physical impact on the environment. 
(CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)(4).)

AGREEMENT
This Agreement (“Agreement”) is entered into as of this __ day of March, 2026 (“Effective 
Date”) by and between the City of San Mateo (“San Mateo”) and the City of Foster City/Estero 
Municipal Improvement District (“Foster City”), referred to herein collectively as the “Parties” 
and individually as a “Party.”
RECITALS
A. In 2023, San Mateo began using its Sewer Enterprise reserve funds to front Foster City’s 
share of WWTP construction costs while the Parties waited for an additional source of 
funds to become available under the State Revolving Fund (“SRF”).  It was thought that 
SRF funds would become quickly available, but it took approximately two years.
B. San Mateo fronted approximately $40.97 million in cash to pay for Foster City’s share of 
construction costs.  Foster City repaid these funds, but has not yet reimbursed San Mateo 
for the foregone interest which San Mateo would have otherwise earned on these 
payments.  
C. In the interests of compromise, the Parties have agreed that Foster City shall repay San 
Mateo for foregone interest on a portion of the aforementioned payments in the amount 
of $148,141.70.  
WHEREFORE, for valuable consideration, including the obligations and terms as set forth 
below, the Parties agree as follows:
1. The foregoing recitals are incorporated herein by reference and shall constitute a part of 
this Agreement.  
2. Foster City agrees to pay San Mateo in the amount of One Hundred Forty-Eight 
Thousand One Hundred and Forty One Dollars and Seventy Cents ($148,141.70) within 
thirty (30) days of the Effective Date, which the Parties agree shall fully and finally 
resolve any claim San Mateo has regarding interest owed related to the matter referenced 
in the recitals.  
3. This Agreement contains the entire agreement and understanding between the Parties 
concerning the subject matter herein and supersedes and replaces any prior negotiations 
and agreements between the Parties, whether written or oral.
4. This Agreement, and the documents referred to herein, are governed by, and construed 
and interpreted in accordance with, the laws of the State of California.  
5. This Agreement may be executed in any number of counterparts, each of which may be 
deemed an original, and all of which together constitute a single instrument, 
notwithstanding that all the Parties are not signatories to the original or same counterpart. 
Photocopies or facsimiles constitute good evidence of such execution.

SUBJECT:
Citywide Capital Project Appropriation Amendments — Adoption
RECOMMENDATION:
Adopt two Resolutions to adjust appropriations for certain Citywide Capital Improvement Program projects.
BACKGROUND:
As part of preparing for the development of the five-year capital improvement program (CIP) for FY 2026-31, staff within 
the Finance, Parks and Recreation, and Public Works Departments completed reviews of existing capital improvement 
projects. Staff identified several projects that needed some type of correction or an appropriation to balance the project 
due to updated costs and/or project timelines. At the same time, City staff identified certain high priority projects that 
needed additional funding within this fiscal year. This report summarizes the recommended appropriations and transfers 
to correct and balance existing projects and provide new funding to projects with immediate needs. All the proposed 
appropriation amendments are also listed in Exhibit A as part of the proposed resolutions (Attachments 1 and 2).  Two 
resolutions are proposed to facilitate recusal of one Council member from voting on appropriations related to the Seal 
Point Park Replacement Well and a restroom remodel at Ryder Park due to the proximity of the Council member’s real 
property interest.
High Priority Projects
•
3rd and Norfolk Traffic Signal - (Project 461214)
On January 13, 2025, City Council awarded a contract to improve safety at the intersection of 3rd Avenue and 
Norfolk Street. This project will modify the intersection of 3rd Ave. and Norfolk St. to improve pedestrian and 
bicycle safety, especially for people using the 3rd Ave. overcrossing of Highway 101. City staff is transferring about 
$213,000 in additional funds to this project from private developer contributions allocated for the work to be 
completed at this intersection from the E 3rd/Norfolk Intersection Reconstruction project (466608) and 
appropriating an additional $50,000 in Measure A funding. 
•
Complete Streets North Central - (Project #46r015)
At the February 2 City Council meeting regarding the Humboldt bike lanes, Council directed staff to proceed 
forward with two efforts. Staff is recommending the appropriation of $225,000 from the General Fund and 
$75,000 from Measure A to address the items listed below in Effort No.1

Effort No. 1 – To immediately implement speed calming improvements on Humboldt Street (per 
presentation), Streetlighting upgrades and exploration of a focused RPPP program

Effort No. 2 – Explore whether converting Humboldt Street into a one-way street is feasible.
In addition, staff is recommending to appropriate $255,000 in General Fund to reimburse the project for the 
additional expenses that were incurred as part of the Humboldt Bike Lanes Alternative Project. 
50 of 424

--- page 51 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
•
Citywide Engineering and Traffic Survey Update – new project
Staff is recommending an appropriation of $180,000 from the General Fund for a new project titled Citywide 
Engineering and Traffic Survey Update. This project will conduct comprehensive engineering and traffic surveys 
(E&TS) across San Mateo's roadways in compliance with the California Vehicle Code and the California Manual for 
Setting Speed Limits. This is a City Council priority which Public Works staff are targeting to complete by summer 
2026.
•
Seal Point Park Replacement Well – new project
The City maintains a closed landfill that requires ongoing environmental monitoring in accordance with regulatory 
permits. The leachate monitoring well LW-4 is no longer functional preventing the collection of samples and 
measurement of leachate elevations. LW-4 is one of five wells used to monitor leachate conditions within the 
landfill, and its failure prevents monitoring in this area from being conducted in accordance with permit 
requirements. Replacement of the well is necessary to maintain ongoing leachate monitoring and program 
compliance. The project is a high priority and will involve properly removing the existing well casing and installing a 
new monitoring well nearby. This condition was not anticipated at the time of budget adoption and requires mid-
year funding to address. The $60,000 in funding needed for this project will come from the Landfill Fund.
Clean-up Projects

Joinville Pool Assessment and Improvements (Project #46f037)
This project was initially planned to implement capital improvements to the Joinville Swim Center including 
accessibility, interior, pool deck, mechanical, electrical, and plumbing improvements. An investigation of a leak in 
the pool shell revealed water infiltration at the bottom of the pool. The scope of the recommended additional 
exploratory work to further assess the leak and related impacts was beyond the scope of the project. Instead, the 
filtration system, pool heaters, and boilers were identified for replacement to extend the life of the pool through 
and a feasibility study is planned to develop a long-term solution for the site. This action will release $2,300,000 in 
General Fund funding from the project to align the budget with current anticipated funding needs.

Enterprise Resource Planning Software (Project #200001)
The implementation of the City’s new Enterprise Resource Planning Software (ERP) is complete. All the contract 
changes have been approved, but the final funding was never appropriated to the ERP project. This appropriates 
$390,676 to the project from the City’s Equipment Replacement Fund to balance and close the project.

Police Department Roof Improvements (Project #46F027)
The completion of a new roof with positive drainage over the Police headquarters building exceeded the project 
budget by $21,242. This appropriates the remaining funding needed from the General Fund to balance and close 
the project.

Park Restroom Phase IV (Project #46F002) and Park Restroom Phase V (Project #46F015)
The Park Restroom Phase IV and Phase V projects included restroom remodels at the Harborview, Ryder, 
Shoreview, and Lakeshore parks and were completed last fiscal year. The balancing adjustments to close these 
projects as part of the 2025-26 budget development process were incorrectly applied between these two projects. 
This action releases $105,000 in excess General Fund funding from the Phase IV project and appropriates $104,999 
in General Fund funding to the Phase V project to balance and close the projects.

ADA Entry Compliance - Beresford (Project #460058)
The design and installation of a compliant ADA access route from the parking lot to the front door of the Beresford 
Recreation Center exceeded the project budget requiring additional funding. This appropriates $5,999 from the 
General Fund to balance the project.
•
Delaware Safe Routes to School Corridor (Project #46R022)
This project is planned to improve the bike infrastructure from Pacific to 19th Avenue, an essential corridor to 
connect the community to schools, transit, and work along S. Delaware Street. The project is funded through a 
51 of 424

--- page 52 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
California Transportation Commission (CTC) grant and a local match of Measure A funding. The grant budget was 
incorrectly duplicated as part of the budget development process and this action reduces the CTC grant budget by 
$1,500,000 to align the budget with the approved grant allocation.

Bermuda Drive Bridge Replacement (Project #462250)
This project will replace the existing Bermuda Drive Bridge in accordance with recommendations in the Caltrans 
bridge inspection report and upgrade the bridge to current standards. The project includes Federal Bridge 
Replacement and Rehabilitation funding through Caltrans in the amount of $6,564,689. This action increases the 
grant budget by $376,189 to align the budget with the approved total grant allocation.

Basins 2 & 3 Collection System Improvements (Project #46s003) 
This correction updates a portion of the funding allocation to this project by reducing the funding from the Sewer 
Fund and increasing the allocation from the South Trunk Fee funding by $1,169,759.47.

Hillsdale Corridor Improvements (Project #462249)
This project includes the design and construction of long-term improvements on the Hillsdale/US-101 bridge, 
including widening eastbound Hillsdale Boulevard from the easterly bridge deck to the US-101 northbound off-
ramp. Additional private developer contributions for this project have been received but were not previously 
recognized in the project budget. As the overall project budget amount has not changed, this action will 
appropriate this $125,000 private developer contribution and will release budgeted Measure A funding from the 
project in a commensurate amount.
BUDGET IMPACT:
The adjustments to the Citywide capital improvement projects include changes to General Fund, Sewer Fund, Landfill 
Fund, Measure A, South Trunk Fee and private developer contribution funding sources as well as grant allocations. The 
changes overall release $1,612,760 to the General Fund which can be available for allocation as part of the upcoming five-
year capital improvement program for FY 2026-2031.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This Resolution to adjust appropriations for certain capital improvement projects is not a project subject to CEQA, because 
it consists of a government fiscal activity that does not involve any commitment to any specific project which may result in 
a potentially significant physical impact on the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)(4).)  Each individual 
project described in this Agenda Report and Proposed Resolution has/will be individually reviewed under CEQA.

SUBJECT:
Microsoft Enterprise Agreement Subscription Increase — Approval
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve a subscription increase to the City’s Enterprise Agreement (EA) with Microsoft for Office software, Windows 
desktop operating systems, and server products for Year 3 of the existing three-year agreement in the amount of 
$28,604.24, for a new total of $794,341.24; and authorize the Director of Information Technology to execute the 
subscription increase in substantially the form presented. 
BACKGROUND:
The City established its Enterprise Agreement (EA) relationship with Microsoft in March of 2007 and last renewed it in 
January 2024, when the Council authorized an expenditure of $765,737. The EA includes desktop operating systems, 
software, and Microsoft cloud services like Teams, Outlook, and SharePoint. As part of the current EA, the City must report 
annually on Microsoft licensing and usage from the prior year including increases to licensing to support new users, in 
order to evaluate whether a higher annual subscription fee is needed. In accordance with the EA, the subscription for each 
year may be adjusted based on that reported usage. Given increases in user licensing to support additional headcount, the 
agreement will cost $28,604.24 more than originally agreed upon, for a new total payment in Year 3 of $271,965. To 
support this increase in licensing, City staff recommends approving the Year 3 Quote Confirmation (Attachment 1) for a 
total agreement amount of $794,341.24. 
BUDGET IMPACT:
The agreed subscription fees for each year for the Microsoft EA were $255,245.92, and equivalent funds were included in 
the Information Technology Department's operating budget. For fiscal year 2024, the amount paid was $255,245.92. For 
fiscal year 2025, the amount paid was $267,130.24. This left a remainder of $243,360.84 in authorized expenditure from 
the $765,737 originally approved in 2024. The subscription fee for Year 3 is $271,965, resulting in a shortfall in Year 3 (FY 
25-26) of $28,604.24. Given budget savings in other areas, the Information Technology Department can absorb the 
additional cost of $28,604.24 for the subscription fee for FY 25-26 within the Department's existing operating budget.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This subscription fee is not a project subject to CEQA, because it can be seen with certainty that it will not cause a physical 
change in the environment. (Public Resources Code Section 21065.)
NOTICE PROVIDED
All meeting noticing requirements were met.

City Council
FROM:
Alex Khojikian, City Manager
PREPARED BY:
Information Technology Department
MEETING DATE:
March 16, 2026 
SUBJECT:
Customer Relationship Management Software and Services — Amendment
RECOMMENDATION:
Approve Amendment No. 1 to the agreement with Catalis Public Works & Citizen Engagement, LLC to increase agreement 
by $10,000, for a revised total agreement amount of $150,500; establish a contingency reserve in the amount of $11,000; 
and authorize the  Director of the Information Technology Department to execute the agreement amendment in 
substantially the form presented and approve any amendments within the contingency amount.
BACKGROUND:
City Council established a Council priority to explore the implementation of a Customer Relationship Management (CRM) 
system. After a competitive request for proposals process, on August 18, 2025, City Council approved an agreement with 
Catalis Public Works & Citizen, Engagement, LLC (Catalis) for a CRM software system for an amount of $140,500 for a 
three-year term. 
Since project launch, staff have worked with City departments to establish workflows and processes incorporating the new 
CRM. Currently, the City uses a contractor to address graffiti in the right-of-way. A separate, backend environment is 
necessary to allow the City’s graffiti contractor to seamlessly access service requests in the new CRM without allowing the 
contractor to access all the City’s service requests. 
Catalis will develop the separate, backend environment, assign a dedicated customer success manager, conduct training 
and provide a one-year annual subscription for $10,000. Future years require an additional annual fee of $5,000 plus 
Consumer Price Index (CPI). The requested contingency in the amount of $11,000 will allow the City to exercise the 
optional one-year extensions for this additional service for the remainder of the agreement term. Based on this 
information, staff recommends City Council approve Amendment No. 1 to the agreement with Catalis and establish a 
contingency reserve in the amount of $11,000. 
BUDGET IMPACT:
There is sufficient funding within the Public Works Field Maintenance and Facilities operating budgets in the General, 
Downtown Services, and Facilities and Fleet Maintenance funds for the agreement amendment and the requested 
contingency.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
Approval of Amendment No. 1 to the City’s Agreement with Catalis Public Works & Citizen Engagement, LLC for additional 
services to integrate graffiti tracking services for the City’s graffiti abatement contractor to the City’ CRM system is not a 
project subject to CEQA, because it can be seen with certainty that there is no possibility that these additional services 
may have a significant effect on the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15061(b)(3).)

STUDY SESSION
1.
Fiscal Year 2025-26 Mid-Year Budget — Update
Abby Veeser, Finance Director, presented the Fiscal Year 2025–26 mid-year budget update to the City 
Council.
Public Comment: Thomas Morgan asked whether previously reported State Controller findings regarding 
excess ERAF calculations had been resolved and whether any impacts to the City remained.
Councilmembers asked questions and discussed vehicle license fee (VLF) revenue projections, volatility in 
real property transfer tax revenues, General Fund reserve policies, frozen positions and related cost savings, 
and ongoing regional advocacy efforts related to VLF funding. Staff also outlined the upcoming budget 
development schedule, noting that the Fiscal Year 2026–28 Budget is currently being prepared and will be 
brought to the City Council for review, including a Budget Study Session and preview of the five-year Capital 
Improvement Plan on April 20, followed by the first public hearing on June 1 and the second public hearing 
on June 15. The City Council received the report and provided feedback to staff; no formal action was taken.

the zoning code update reflects neighborhood character and livability considerations, and incorporate climate 
resilience considerations such as sea level rise. Council also encouraged staff to simplify and clarify survey 
questions and public outreach materials, provide flexibility within development standards, and pursue

throughout the code, and continuing robust community engagement as the project advances.

SUBJECT:
 Temporary Sign Placement Enforcement Policy During Election Periods — Adoption
RECOMMENDATION:
Adopt a Resolution to approve the Temporary Sign Placement Enforcement During Elections Policy to standardize 
guidelines for the City's enforcement of temporary signs in accordance with San Mateo Municipal Code Title 25 (Signs) and 
authorize the City Manager to make non-substantive changes as needed. 
BACKGROUND:
Campaign signs are regulated by San Mateo Municipal Code Title 25 (Signs), which establishes standards governing the 
placement, size, location, and manner of signs within the City. These provisions are content-neutral time, place, and 
manner regulations intended to preserve community aesthetics, maintain pedestrian and traffic safety, and protect free 
speech rights consistent with the First Amendment.
During the February 18, 2025, City Council discussion regarding campaign contribution limits, Council members raised 
concerns about the visibility, placement, and enforcement of signage during the 2024 election cycle. At that meeting, 
Council directed staff to return with a proposed administrative policy to clarify enforcement practices and enhance 
outreach to candidates and the community regarding how the City responds to sign violations, including temporary signs 
during election campaigns.
The proposed policy (Attachment 1) responds to that direction by establishing a standardized administrative framework 
for enforcement of the existing Sign Ordinance. The policy does not amend the Municipal Code or create new regulatory 
requirements. Instead, it clarifies how the Sign Ordinance will be implemented, communicated, and coordinated across 
City departments during election cycles.  Additionally, as part of an upcoming update to the Master Fee Schedule, staff 
plans to include a fee to retrieve signs unlawfully placed either on public property or in the public right-of-way. This fee, 
which would pay for the City's reasonable costs to impound and store the sign(s), is already authorized by Section 
25.08.010(d)(2) of the Sign Ordinance.  
During the 2024 election cycle, the City Clerk’s Office received more than sixty complaints related to sign placement. Staff 
found that the broader Sign Ordinance, while comprehensive, can be difficult for candidates, campaign committees, and 
members of the public to interpret as it applies specifically to signage. In addition, the absence of a standardized 
enforcement framework created uncertainty regarding complaint intake, interdepartmental coordination, and the process 
for removal and impoundment of noncompliant signs.
The proposed policy addresses these challenges by clarifying departmental responsibilities, establishing a consistent 
complaint intake process, and outlining the City’s enforcement procedures.
80 of 424

--- page 81 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
Under the policy, the City Clerk’s Office will serve as the primary intake point for sign complaints, receiving and 
documenting reports submitted by the public and coordinating communication between complainants, campaign 
committees, and City departments. The Clerk’s Office will also distribute educational materials regarding sign regulations 
to candidates and campaign committees and maintain public-facing guidance summarizing the City’s sign rules during 
election cycles.
The Code Enforcement Division will assist with field verification of potential violations and may issue courtesy notices or 
formal notifications when violations occur. When signs placed on public property or within the public right-of-way are 
determined to be in violation of the Sign Ordinance, Public Works staff will assist with the removal, transport, and storage 
of impounded signs, consistent with the enforcement provisions of the Municipal Code.
Together, these procedures establish a clear and coordinated process for complaint intake, verification, and enforcement, 
while providing candidates, campaign committees, and the public clearer guidance regarding the City’s campaign sign 
regulations and enforcement practices. 
BUDGET IMPACT:
There is no budgetary impact associated with the adoption of the proposed Resolution.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This policy is not a project subject to CEQA, because it can be seen with certainty that it will not cause a physical change in 
the environment. (Public Resources Code Section 21065.)
NOTICE PROVIDED
All meeting noticing requirements were met.

TEMPORARY SIGN PLACEMENT ENFORCEMENT DURING ELECTIONS POLICY 
 
WHEREAS, signs are regulated by San Mateo Municipal Code Title 25 (Signs) (hereafter, the “Sign 
Ordinance”), which establishes standards governing the placement, size, location, and manner of signs within 
the City; and); and 
 
WHEREAS, the Sign Ordinance establishes content-neutral time, place, and manner regulations intended 
to preserve community aesthetics, maintain pedestrian and traffic safety, and protect free speech rights 
consistent with the First Amendment to the United States Constitution; and 
 
WHEREAS, during election cycles, the City receives inquiries and complaints related to the placement of 
signs, and consistent enforcement of the Sign Ordinance requires coordination among multiple City 
departments; and 
 
WHEREAS, on February 18, 2025, during its discussion regarding campaign contribution limits, the City 
Council directed staff to explore the development of an administrative policy to clarify enforcement practices 
and improve public understanding of the City’s sign regulations; and 
 
WHEREAS, the proposed Temporary Sign Placement Enforcement During Elections Policy establishes 
standardized administrative procedures for complaint intake, verification of potential violations, and 
coordination of enforcement actions under the existing Sign Ordinance; and 
 
NOW, THEREFORE, THE CITY COUNCIL OF THE CITY OF SAN MATEO, CALIFORNIA, HEREBY RESOLVES 
that:  
 
1. This policy adoption is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is an organizational or 
administrative activity that will not result in direct or indirect physical changes in the environment. 
(CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)(5).) 
 
2. The Temporary Sign Placement Enforcement During Elections Policy attached as Exhibit A to this 
Resolution is approved and the City Manager is authorized to make non-substantive changes.

EXHIBIT A 
 
Title: 
Temporary Sign Placement Enforcement During 
Elections Policy 
Policy #: 
118 
Sponsored by: 
City Clerk’s Office 
Approved by: 
City Council 
Date: 
Issued: __/__/____ 
Amended: __/__/____ 
Purpose 
This policy establishes standardized guidelines for the City’s enforcement of San Mateo Municipal 
Code (SMMC) Title 25 (Signs) (hereafter, the “Sign Ordinance”), as it specifically relates to temporary 
signs within city limits. 
Policy 
 
The Sign Ordinance establishes standards governing the placement, size, location, and manner of 
signs within the City. Signs that are installed or maintained in violation of the Sign Ordinance, including 
but not limited to Chapters 25.04 (Signs on Public Property and in the Public Right-of-Way), 25.06 
(Signs on Private Property), and 25.08 (Prohibited, Illegal, and Non-Conforming Signs, are subject to 
enforcement action in accordance with the municipal code. These include signs commonly displayed 
during election campaigns, referred to herein for convenience as “temporary signs.”  
 
Except where a sign is prohibited or otherwise unlawful under the Sign Ordinance, this policy does not 
restrict an individual’s ability to place a temporary sign on private property they own or lawfully control, 
and is not intended to regulate the content of signs, including political speech. The provisions of the 
Sign Ordinance are content-neutral time, place, and manner regulations, adopted to preserve 
community aesthetics, as well as traffic and pedestrian safety, while protecting free speech rights in 
accordance with the First Amendment to the United States Constitution, among other purposes 
identified in SMMC section 25.02.010.  
Refer to the Sign Ordinance for applicable restrictions and definitions. See Exhibit 1 for excerpts most 
applicable to temporary signage.   
Scope 
This policy shall apply to all city employees, unless a department policy addresses the same subject. If 
there is a conflict between the requirements of this policy or the procedures implementing the policy 
and the department’s policy, the more restrictive shall apply, unless compliance with the more 
restrictive requirement would conflict with applicable law.  
Responsibility  
83 of 424

--- page 84 ---
118 –Temporary Sign Placement Enforcement During Elections 
 
Page 2 of 12 
3/16/2026 
 
1. City Clerk’s Office 
A. Receive and record complaints regarding temporary signs, either directly (e.g., via email 
or phone) or through a web-based complaint form. Record: date/time received, location, 
photos (if provided), complainant contact (if any), and alleged issue (ROW/private 
property/visibility/attachment, etc.). 
B. Serve as the primary point of contact between: the complainant, the impacted campaign 
committee (if applicable and when identifiable), and City staff responsible for verification 
and/or removal/impoundment. 
 
 
C. Distribute this policy and an informal Code Enforcement courtesy notice to each active 
campaign committee operating within the City (e.g., upon filing/identification as active) 
and maintain a record of distribution.   
D. Maintain public-facing educational information on the City’s website (e.g., “Temporary 
Sign Rules”) that summarizes the City’s content-neutral time/place/manner sign 
regulations under the Sign Ordinance, including key restrictions for signs in the public 
right-of-way (Chapter 25.04) and prohibitions under Chapter 25.08. 
E. Coordinate periodic election-season reminders to campaign committees and the public. 
2. Code Enforcement Division 
A. Assist with field verification of potential violations of the Sign Ordinance, including: 
whether the sign appears to be in the public right-of-way and subject to Chapter 25.04 
restrictions; whether the sign appears to meet prohibited conditions under SMMC 
section 25.08.010(a)–(b) (e.g., no consent, prohibited locations, visibility/ingress-egress 
hazards); and whether immediate action is warranted due to safety concerns (unsafe 
sign condition consistent with SMMC section 25.08.010(c)(2)) 
B. Prepare a formal courtesy notice from the Code Enforcement Division to be distributed 
to campaign committees and violators. 
C. When signs require immediate removal/impoundment (e.g., signs in the ROW in 
violation of the Sign Ordinance), assist with or coordinate collection support consistent 
with SMMC section 25.08.010(d)(2). 
D. Issue formal notifications on Code Enforcement letterhead to address repeat violations 
of the municipal code. 
3. Public Works Department 
A. Once the City Clerk’s Office or Code Enforcement Division has identified a violation, the 
Public Works Department will assist with the collection, transport, and impoundment of 
signs that are removed from public property or the public right-of-way pursuant to SMMC 
section 25.08.010(d)(2). 
B. Maintain or coordinate an impound storage process consistent with SMMC section 
25.08.010(d)(2) (e.g., holding period, inventory, and disposal process after a minimum of 
10 days’ notice), and provide inventory details to the City Clerk’s Office and Code

Enforcement to support owner notification efforts, including retrieval after the appropriate 
impounding time has elapsed. 
Procedures 
1. Violation Criteria 
A. Refer to the Sign Ordinance for applicable restrictions and definitions. See Exhibit 1 for 
excerpts most applicable to temporary signage.   
2. Reporting and Intake 
A. Complaint Intake 
a) The City Clerk’s Office is responsible for receiving and documenting temporary 
sign complaints submitted by members of the public or City staff. 
b) Complaints should include location, description of the sign, date observed, and 
photographs. 
c) Signs deemed to be in violation of the Sign Ordinance and this policy will be 
removed without notice. 
B. Recordkeeping 
a) Maintain a log of reported violations, including referral status and resolution. 
C. Referral 
a) The City Clerk’s Office will refer reported violations to Code Enforcement, with 
City Attorney’s Office support, as needed, for verification and follow-up. 
3. Enforcement Process 
A. Education and Awareness:  
a) The City Clerk’s office shall provide a copy of this policy to candidates, and active 
committees to advise of the temporary sign placement rules, reporting 
procedures and enforcement process. 
B. Verification:

3/16/2026 
 
a) Code Enforcement Division, in coordination with the City Clerk’s Office, will verify 
reported violations to determine whether the sign complies with the Sign 
Ordinance. 
b) Enforcement of sign regulations is generally complaint driven, however City staff 
may identify signs in violation of the Sign Ordinance during routine inspections or 
while performing official duties.  
C. Violations on Private Property 
a) Code Enforcement, in coordination with the City Clerk’s Office, may contact the 
property owner or lawful occupant to confirm whether permission was granted for 
the placement of the temporary sign. 
b) Upon verification of a violation, if that violation is not cured by the property owner 
or person responsible for the installation or maintenance of the sign, Code 
Enforcement may issue a formal notice of violation.  
D. Violations on Public Property or in the Public Right-of-Way 
a) Immediate Removal 
i. 
Pursuant to SMMC section 25.08.010(d)(2), any temporary sign placed 
on public property or within the public right-of-way in violation of the Sign 
Ordinance may be removed and impounded without prior notice. 
ii. 
Code Enforcement, with assistance from Public Works staff, will 
coordinate removal and transport of the sign and place it in a dedicated 
storage area. 
b) Impounding and Retrieval  
i. 
Removed signs must be held for a minimum of thirty (30) days. 
4. After notice is provided, the owner has ten (10) days to retrieve the sign and pay the fee for 
retrieval and storage, as determined by City Council. 
i. 
During this period, the City will make reasonable efforts to notify the sign 
owner or responsible party, if identifiable. 
ii. 
If the sign is not retrieved within that timeframe, the City may dispose of 
the sign at its discretion.

Chapter 25.02 GENERAL PROVISIONS 
25.02.010 PURPOSE. 
The intent of this Title is to provide standards for the regulation of signs in order to: 
(a) Protect and enhance the visual and aesthetic character of residential neighborhoods, 
business areas, and all zoning districts by prohibiting the visual clutter of obtrusive and 
incompatible signs; 
(b) Allow for reasonable and equitable identification of businesses and properties; and 
(c) Protect free speech rights in accordance with the First Amendment to the United States 
Constitution. 
25.02.030 DEFINITIONS. 
(i) Freestanding Sign. A sign which is self-supporting in a fixed location and not attached to or 
projecting over any building. 
… 
(v) Private Property. Property other than Public Property or Public Right-of-Way. 
… 
(x) Public Property. Property owned by the City, but excluding Public Right of Way. 
(y) Public Right-of-Way. That area or those areas dedicated to public use for public street purposes 
including, but not limited to, roadways, parkways, alleys, and sidewalks. 
… 
(bb) Sign. Any structure, display, device, balloon or graphic placed on any land, building or structure, 
which is used to communicate any message, or which advertises or promotes any business, 
product, activity, person or interest. Signs include, but are not limited to, any writing, pictorial 
representation, logo, symbol, banner, or any other figure of similar character of whatever 
material which is used to identify, announce, direct attention to, advertise or communicate, 
which is not inside a building. The term "placed" shall include constructing, erecting, posting, 
painting, printing, tacking, nailing, gluing, sticking, carving, stringing, or otherwise fastening, 
affixing, or making visible in any manner whatsoever. Notwithstanding the general scope of the 
foregoing, the following shall not be deemed to be signs for the purposes of this Title 
… 
(cc) Sign Area. The area in square feet within the smallest rectangle enclosing the total exterior 
surface of a sign or one face of a "double faced sign". Sign area for a multi-faced sign that has 
an angle between sides of the sign that exceeds 30 degrees shall be counted for all sides. 
Where the lettered or illustrated material of a sign consists of individual letters or if the message 
surface consists of noncontiguous segments or has an irregularly shaped perimeter, then the 
area of the sign shall be all of the area encompassed within a single continuous rectilinear-
89 of 424

--- page 90 ---
118 –Temporary Sign Placement Enforcement During Elections 
 
Page 8 of 12 
3/16/2026 
 
perimeter of not more than six straight lines, including any color, material or graphic which is 
integrated therein which differentiates the message from the background. 
… 
(ee) Temporary Sign. A sign to be displayed only for a limited time as specified by this 
Chapter. A temporary sign includes a temporary banner. 
Chapter 25.04 SIGNS ON PUBLIC PROPERTY AND IN THE PUBLIC RIGHT-OF-WAY 
25.04.010 FINDINGS. 
In enacting this Chapter, the City Council finds: 
(a) If carefully regulated, the placement of signs on city sidewalks by private individuals can 
provide a useful outlet for the expression of ideas and the communication of information 
related to beneficial commercial activity, including, but not limited to, the advertisement of 
real estate open house events. 
(b) It is the desire of the City Council to enact standards that would allow for the regulated use 
of city sidewalks for these communication purposes. 
(c) In enacting these regulations it is not the intention of the City Council to regulate the content 
of messages on signs to be placed on city sidewalks, but, instead, it is the City Council's 
intention to enact reasonable time, place and manner restrictions aimed at insuring the safety of 
those using the public sidewalks and those driving on adjacent streets, and to achieve the City's 
aesthetic interests by reducing visual clutter that would result from the unregulated posting of 
signs on sidewalks. 
 
25.04.020 RESTRICTIONS APPLICABLE TO SIGNS ON PUBLIC PROPERTY AND IN THE PUBLIC 
RIGHT-OF-WAY 
(a) Except as otherwise provided in this Chapter, it is unlawful for any person other than a City 
representative to place a sign on public property or in the public right-of-way where such sign 
fails to comply with any of the restrictions stated in this section. 
(b) Restrictions Applicable to Signs. 
(1) No sign shall exceed thirty-six inches in height. 
(2) No sign shall exceed six square feet in area. 
(3) All signs shall be constructed or anchored to prevent movement of the sign by the 
wind, except that an anchoring shall not be permanent and shall not damage the 
property on which the sign is placed. 
(c) Restrictions Applicable to the Placement of Signs.

(1) No sign shall be placed during hours of darkness. 
(2) No sign shall be placed within the median of any public street. 
(3) No sign shall be attached to, or leaned against, any street furniture, utility facility 
(including poles and boxes), street light, building, fence, or any other sign. 
(4) No sign shall be placed within 50 feet of any other sign placed under the provisions 
of this chapter, except that as many as 4 signs may be placed on sidewalks within 
50 feet of the intersection of public streets on each corner of such intersections. 
(5) No sign shall be placed in such a manner as to reduce the unobstructed path of 
travel on any sidewalk to less than 36 inches, and if the existing unobstructed path 
of travel of a sidewalk is 36 inches or less, no sign shall be placed on that 
sidewalk. 
(6) No sign shall be placed within a curb cut or ramp installed to provide improved 
access to a sidewalk to the disabled. 
(7) No sign shall be placed upon any public right-of-way other than a public sidewalk, 
except that signs may be placed in unimproved right-of-way with the consent of the

vehicle parked within the public right-of-way. This prohibition shall not apply to signs placed 
within the interior of a vehicle, signs that are painted on a vehicle, or to signs

street so as to obstruct free and clear vision, or obstruct visibility within the 
triangular area of private property formed by the extension of intersection curb 
lines, or pavement edge where no curb exists, and the diagonal line connecting the 
point on each of the two streets at a distance 45 feet back from the intersection. 
(3) Ingress/Egress. No sign shall be erected, relocated or maintained so as to prevent 
free ingress to or egress from any door, window, fire escape or fire equipment. 
(c) Illegal Signs—Nuisance. All illegal signs are expressly declared a nuisance. For purposes of this 
section, an illegal sign shall mean: 
(1) A sign erected and/or maintained without first complying with all ordinances and 
regulations. 
(2) A sign which is a danger to the public or is unsafe. 
(3) A prohibited sign as defined by this title.

(d) Enforcement. 
(1) The placement of a sign on public or private property or in the public right-of-way in 
violation of any provision of this Title may be enforced by any method provided by 
this Code. Each day that the violation continues shall be deemed to be a new 
violation. All violations are declared to be public nuisances. 
(2) Any sign placed on public property or in the public right-of-way in violation of any provision 
of this Title may be removed and impounded without notice. Impounded signs will be 
held for at least 30days. If possible, the City will make reasonable attempts to notify the 
owner of an impounded sign that the sign has been impounded. If after 10 days' notice 
to reclaim the sign, the owner of the sign fails to retrieve the sign and pay the City's 
reasonable costs to impound and store the sign, the sign may be disposed of in any 
manner whatsoever at the City's discretion. The amount of the sign retrieval fee shall be 
established by City Council resolution.

March 16, 2026 
SUBJECT:
Operation of Leaf Blowers — Ordinance Adoption
RECOMMENDATION:
Adopt an Ordinance to amend San Mateo Municipal Code Chapter 10.80 "Operation of Leaf Blowers" to prohibit the use of 
gas leaf blowers. 
BACKGROUND:
On March 2, 2026, the City Council introduced an Ordinance to amend Chapter 10.80 of the San Mateo Municipal Code to 
prohibit the use of gas leaf blowers. The proposed amendment would prohibit the use of gas-powered leaf blowers 
citywide, provide that electric leaf blowers are subject to existing specified hours of operation, and add Juneteenth to the 
list of holidays on which the operation of electric leaf blowers is prohibited. The Ordinance would establish an effective 
date of January 1, 2027, approximately nine months after adoption to allow time for transition. The Ordinance also allows 
for administrative citations to be issued by code enforcement staff to both the operator of a gas leaf blower and the 
property owner who hired or employed services using such equipment.
If adopted, the Ordinance will become effective on January 1, 2027.
BUDGET IMPACT:
The implementation and enforcement of this Ordinance will be integrated into the City’s existing code enforcement 
procedures. On average, the City has issued 23 electric leaf blower rebates and amounting to an average of $3,142 per 
year, supported by the City’s Sustainability Program budget. Staff anticipate budgeting $10,000 per year for electric leaf 
blower equipment and battery replacement in future budget cycles.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This Ordinance Adoption is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is an organizational or administrative activity that will 
not result in direct or indirect physical changes in the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)(5).)
NOTICE PROVIDED
All meeting noticing requirements were met.

CITY OF SAN MATEO
DRAFT ORDINANCE
Amending San Mateo Municipal Code Chapter 10.80 “Operation of Leaf Blowers.”
WHEREAS, gas-powered leaf blowers emit greenhouse gases and other pollutants including carbon 
monoxide, nitrogen oxides and hydrocarbons that are harmful to human health and the environment; and
WHEREAS, research by the California Air Resources Board has identified the use of gas-powered small 
off-road engines, including leaf blowers, as detrimental to the environment as they emit high levels of air 
pollutants like nitrogen oxides and other reactive organic gases; and
WHEREAS, modern, readily available electric leaf blower equipment generally produces less noise and 
air pollution; and
WHEREAS, in 1997, the City Council adopted a leaf blower ordinance to regulate leaf blower use and 
establish hours of operation; and
WHEREAS, the City of San Mateo Climate Action Plan seeks to reduce greenhouse gas emissions 40% 
below 1990 levels by 2030 and 85% below 1990 levels and achieve carbon neutrality by 2045; and
WHEREAS, the City Council seeks to reduce greenhouse gas emissions and air pollution by prohibiting 
the use of gas leaf blowers in San Mateo and modify hours of operation of leaf blower use. 
NOW, THEREFORE, THE COUNCIL OF THE CITY OF SAN MATEO ORDAINS AS FOLLOWS:
Section 1. Section 10.80.010 of the San Mateo Municipal Code is amended as follows:
10.80.010 Purpose.
It has been found that leaf blowers cause considerable noise and air pollution and have been the source 
of numerous complaints by San Mateo residents. This chapter is intended to regulate the use of leaf blowers to 
minimize noise and air pollution in the City.
Section 2. Section 10.80.020 of the San Mateo Municipal Code is amended as follows:
10.80.020 Leaf Blower – Definition.
“Electric leaf blower” is defined as any leaf blower powered by electric means, including but not limited 
to, battery-powered equipment.
“Gas leaf blower” is defined as any leaf blower powered by a combustion engine using gasoline or any 
other liquid or gaseous fluid.
“Leaf blowers” are defined as portable equipment that is powered by a self-contained engine and used 
in any landscape, maintenance, construction, property repair, or property maintenance for the purpose of 
96 of 424

--- page 97 ---
blowing, dispersing or redistributing dust, dirt, leaves, grass, clippings, cuttings and trimmings from trees, shrubs 
or other debris.
Section 3. Section 10.80.025 of the San Mateo Municipal Code is added as follows:
10.80.025 Prohibition of Gas Leaf Blowers.
It shall be unlawful for any person to operate or authorize the operation of a gas leaf blower within the 
city limits.
Section 4. Section 10.80.030 of the San Mateo Municipal Code is amended as follows:
10.80.030 Restriction of Electric Leaf Blowers - Hours of Operation.
No person shall use or operate an electric leaf blower in a residential zoning district or in areas 
bordering a residential zoning district before 8:00 a.m. or after 5:00 p.m. Monday through Friday, nor prior to 
9:00 a.m. or after 5:00 p.m. on Saturdays. Use of electric leaf blowers on Sundays or on the following holidays is 
prohibited: New Years Day, Martin Luther King, Jr. Birthday, Presidents' Day, Memorial Day, Juneteenth, 4th of 
July, Labor Day, Veterans Day, Thanksgiving, Christmas.
Section 5. Section 10.80.060 of the San Mateo Municipal Code is amended as follows:
10.80.060 Violations.
It is unlawful for any person or entity to violate the provisions of this chapter. Enforcement of this 
chapter shall be subject to enforcement pursuant to Title 1 of the San Mateo Municipal Code or any legal 
remedy available by law. Violations of this chapter may be enforced against the leaf blower operator and/or 
property owner who has hired, employed or engaged the services of a person or business utilizing leaf blowers. 
Section 6. Environmental Determination. In accordance with California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA) 
Guidelines Section 15308, this action is categorically exempt from CEQA, because it consists of an action to 
protect the environment by reducing greenhouse gas emissions.
Section 7. Severability. In the event any section, clause or provision of this ordinance shall be determined 
invalid or unconstitutional, such section, clause or provision shall be deemed severable and all other sections or 
portions hereof shall remain in full force and effect.
Section 8. Publication. This Ordinance shall be published in summary in a newspaper of general circulation, 
posted in the City Clerk's Office, and posted on the City's website, all in accord with Section 2.15 of the City 
Charter.
Section 9. Legislative History and Effective Date. This ordinance was introduced on Clerk to complete., and 
adopted on Clerk to complete., and shall be effective on January 1, 2027.
97 of 424

--- page 98 ---
Chapter 10.80
OPERATION OF LEAF BLOWERS
10.80.010 PURPOSE.
It has been found that leaf blowers cause considerable noise and air pollution 
and have been the source of numerous complaints by San Mateo residentscitizens 
living in residential zoning districts. This chapter is intended to regulate the use of leaf 
blowers to minimize noise and air pollution in the City's residentially zoned 
neighborhoods and in areas bordering residentially zoned neighborhoods.
10.80.020 LEAF BLOWER—DEFINITION.
“Electric leaf blower” is defined as any leaf blower powered by electric means, 
including but not limited to, battery-powered equipment.
“Gas leaf blower” is defined as any leaf blower powered by a combustion engine 
using gasoline or any other liquid or gaseous fluid.
“Leaf blowers” are defined as portable equipment that is powered by a self-
contained fuel engine and used in any landscape, maintenance, construction, property 
repair, or property maintenance for the purpose of blowing, dispersing or redistributing 
dust, dirt, leaves, grass, clippings, cuttings and trimmings from trees, shrubs or other 
debris.
10.80.025 PROHIBITION OF GAS LEAF BLOWERS.
It shall be unlawful for any person to operate or authorize the operation of a gas 
leaf blower within the city limits.
10.80.030 RESTRICTION OF ELECTRIC LEAF BLOWERS - HOURS OF OPERATION.
No person shall use or operate aan electric leaf blower in a residential zoning district or 
in areas bordering a residential zoning district before 8:00 a.m. or after 5:00 p.m. 
Monday through Friday, nor prior to 9:00 a.m. or after 5:00 p.m. on Saturdays. Use of 
electric leaf blowers on Sundays or on the following holidays is prohibited: New Years 
Day, Martin Luther King, Jr. Birthday, Presidents' Day, Memorial Day, Juneteenth, 4th of 
July, Labor Day, Veterans Day, Thanksgiving, Christmas.
10.80.040
LIMITATIONS ON USE.
Any person who uses or operates a leaf blower in a residential zoning district or 
in areas bordering a residential zoning district shall use a blower nozzle extension and 
98 of 424

--- page 99 ---
shall run the blower at a low speed to minimize noise. No more than one blower shall be 
operated at a residence at any time.
10.80.050 REMOVAL OF DEBRIS.
No material or matter blown by leaf blowers shall be blown upon neighboring 
properties or onto any portion of the public right-of-way, including but not limited to 
sidewalks and streets, without being immediately removed.
10.80.060 VIOLATIONS.
It is unlawful for any person or entity to violate the provisions of this chapter. 
Enforcement of this chapter shall be subject to enforcement pursuant to Title 1 of the 
San Mateo Municipal Code or any legal remedy available by law. Violations of this 
chapter may be enforced against the leaf blower operator and/or property owner who 
has hired, employed or engaged the services of a person or business utilizing leaf 
blowers. 
10.80.070 CONSTRUCTION.
No section of this chapter shall impose a mandatory duty on the City, or on any 
officer, official, agent, employee, board, council, or commission of the City. Instead, if 
any section purports to impose a mandatory duty of enforcement, that section shall be 
deemed to invest the City, and the appropriate officer, official, agent, employee, board, 
council, or commission with discretion to enforce the section or not to enforce it.

SUBJECT:
Reach Codes for the 2025 Code Cycle — Ordinance Adoption
RECOMMENDATION:
Adopt an Ordinance to amend San Mateo Municipal Code Chapter 23.24 "Energy Code" to require energy conservation 
measures for air conditioner alterations, replacements and installations in single family homes, duplexes and townhomes; 
energy conservation measures for heating, ventilation and air conditioner replacements and installations in nonresidential 
buildings; and increased efficiency and electric readiness requirements for additions and alterations to single family 
homes, duplexes, and townhomes.
BACKGROUND:
On March 2, 2026, the City Council introduced an Ordinance to amend Chapter 23.24, “Energy Code,” of the San Mateo 
Municipal Code to require energy conservation measures for air conditioner alterations, replacements, and installations in 
single-family homes, duplexes, and townhomes; energy conservation measures for heating, ventilation, and air conditioner 
replacements and installations in nonresidential buildings; and increased efficiency and electric readiness requirements for 
additions and alterations to single-family homes, duplexes, and townhomes.
The Ordinance requirements focus on specific project opportunities to encourage building electrification and energy 
efficiency when work is already voluntarily being completed. 
If adopted, the Ordinance will become effective 30 days after adoption. 
BUDGET IMPACT:
There is no budget impact.
ENVIRONMENTAL DETERMINATION:
This Ordinance Adoption is not a project subject to CEQA, because it is an organizational or administrative activity that will 
not result in direct or indirect physical changes in the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)(5).)

WHEREAS, the City of San Mateo’s (City) Climate Action Plan recommends the City review local
