H1.10 Establish By-Right 
Housing Designation for 
Prior Housing Sites
Amend the Zoning Code to establish a By-Right designation for housing sites reused 
from prior Housing Elements for housing projects that propose a minimum of 20% 
affordable units. Zoning for these sites must be at least 30 units/acre to meet default 
density requirements for lower-income households per Gov. Code Section 65583.2(c).
12/31/2024
6th Cycle
Completed
On July 15, 2024, the City Council adopted Ordinance No. 2024-4 adding 
Chapter 27.94 Housing Opportunities Overlay District (H) to the Zoning 
Code. The (H) Overlay establishes a Housing By-Right designation for 
housing sites reused from prior Housing Elements for housing projects 
that propose a minimum of 20% affordable units. Zoning for these sites 
must be at least 30 units/acre to meet default density requirements for 
lower-income households
Meetings
1
Ordinance 2024-4: 
https://law.cityofsanmateo.org/us/ca/cities/san-
mateo/ordinances/2024/4

H1.14 Update Supportive 
Housing Requirements
Amend the Zoning Code to be consistent with AB 2162 to allow by-right 100% affordable 
housing that has 25% or 12 units of permanent supportive housing, where multi-family 
or mixed-use housing is permitted. 
12/31/2024
6th Cycle
Completed
On April 7, 2025, the City Council adopted an ordinance to update the 
zoning code that added a provision to R3 zoning districts stating that 
supportive housing in compliance with Government Code Sections 
65650 - 65656, shall be considered a use by-right use. "Use by right" 
shall have the same meaning as defined in Government Code Section 
65583.2(i). The R3 permitted uses are enumerated in other multi-family 
residential and mixed-use districts.

H1.16 Update Farmworker 
Housing Requirements
Amend the Zoning Code to define and allow farmworker housing within the Agricultural 
District consistent with Government Code Section 17021.6. The City will comply with 
Health and Safety Code section 17021.5.
12/31/2025
6th Cycle
Completed
On April 7, 2025, the City Council adopted an ordinance to add a 
definiton section (27.060.020) in Chapter 27.60 Special Districts, Article I 
Agricultural Districts and adding the term 'farmworker housing' and 
include the defintions of farmworker housing from Health and Safety 
Code Sections 17021.5 and 17021.6.  Farmworker housing up to 36 beds 
in group quarters (or 12 units or less) was added as a permitted use 
under Agricultural Districts (Section 27.60.030). Temporary farmworker 
housing consisting of more than 36 beds in a group quarters or more 
than 12 units or spaces designed for use by a single family or household 
was added as a special use under Section 27.60.040.

H1.20 Adopt San Mateo 
General Plan 2040
a)   Complete the General Plan 2040 Update (GPU) process and present to the City 
Council for adoption. The City is committed to adopting a General Plan that will create 
capacity for at least 10,000 new housing units and will increase the base densities in the 
10 Study Areas by at least 25 du/ac and height limits by at least two stories. 
12/31/2024
6th Cycle
Completed
a) On March 18, 2024, the City Council adopted General Plan 2040. The 
Land Use Element established new land use designations and map that 
increases housing capacity by approximately 19,700 new housing units, 
increases base densities to up to 130 du/ac, and increases heights up to 
eight stories.

H2.3 Increase Energy and 
Water Efficiency in 
Existing Units
b)   Implement energy-efficiency and electrification strategies identified in the City's 
Climate Action Plan through updates to the City’s Reach Codes as part of the building 
permit review process. Outreach will be conducted biannually.
12/31/2025
6th Cycle
In Progress
b) The City's updated Reach Codes went into effect, requiring any 
remodel projects to include energy and water efficiency measures. In 
2024, Due to a federal court decision, the City suspended enforcement of 
its Reach Codes that prohibit the installation of new gas infrastructure.  
The Ninth Circuit Court of Appeals in California Restaurant Association 
v. City of Berkeley determined that a local ordinance that generally 
prohibited the installation of natural gas infrastructure was preempted 
by federal law, namely the Energy Policy and Conservation Act (EPCA). 
At a November 3, 2025 City Council meeting, the Council reviewed four 
reach code options that does not require whole home electrification and 
directed staff to develop an ordinance that had all four reach code 
options. The Council is scheduled to consider the draft ordinance in Q1 
2026.
Meetings
1
Reach Code information including updates to 
the Reach Code can be found here: 
https://www.cityofsanmateo.org/3363/Reach-
Codes

H3.4 Expand Tenant

practices for code amendments to extend tenant relocation protections 
to tenants with tenure less than one year. This research was combined 
with researching tenant protection policies for substantial remodel 
evictions as described in b) and strengthened enforcement penalties for 
substanard units in c), in addition to research on a rental registry to 
track rental rates and evictions citywide, as described in Policy H.36.

to implement a) and c). The ordinances became effective Jan 1, 2026.

to collect voluntary information from property owners via the City's 
business tax application platform. Finally, City Council directed staff to 
establish an Emergency Rental Assistance Program funded with local 
funds and administered by a local nonprofit.

Sites Inventory Property 
Owners

conducted within two years of adoption and shall be ongoing throughout the housing 
cycle.

development entitlements. City staff targets quarterly roundtable 
discussions with developers and property owners.

the entire planning period.

H5.2.1:  Add more city 
supported housing with

of affluence.
Require developers to affirmatively market approximately 1,000 units to those with 
disproportionate housing needs over the eight-year period (approximately 125 annually) 
by preparing and submitting and affirmative marketing plan to the City for review. The 
affirmative marketing plan shall include items, such as advertising (print, social media) 
and targeting community organizations that serve households with disproportionate 
housing needs. Ensure that programs target/affirmatively market to households with 
disproportionate housing needs. Of the 1,000 affordable units, approximately 15% will 
benefit special needs and/or ELI households.
Continue to update the housing inventory and provide on the City’s website so that 
developers can target housing in moderate and high opportunity areas, as well as areas 
of affluence.

6th Cycle
In Progress
In Winter 2023, affirmative marketing began for the Kiku Crossing 
affordable housing project as focused outreach was used for units 
aimed at special needs populations through County and local nonprofit 
organizations. Kiku Crossing is located in a Highest Resource area 
defined by the 2024 TCAC Opportunity maps.  
In Fall/Winter 2024, the City worked with MidPen Housing on an 
affirmative marketing plan for vacant units at 2000 S. Delaware, a 
formerly moderate-income affordable housing development on City-
owned land that was acquired by MidPen Housing in 2024 and converted 
to a low-income (80% AMI) housing development, with a City loan of 
$500,000. Application processing continued into 2025. 2000 S. Delaware 
is located in a High Resource area as defined by the 2024 TCAC 
Opportunity Map.
Units
319

submitted affirmative marketing plans for the 
City's approval for both Kiku Crossing and

reach individuals with disproportionate 
housing needs.

Tenant Preference Policy
Local governments are required to inform HCD about any local tenant preference ordinance the local government maintains when the jurisdiction submits their annual progress report on housing approvals and production, per Government 
Code 7061 (SB 649, 2022, Cortese). Effective January 1, 2023, local governments adopting a tenant preference are required to create a webpage on their internet website containing authorizing local ordinance and supporting materials, 
no more than 90 days after the ordinance becomes operational.
https://www.cityofsanmateo.org/DocumentCenter/View/99291/BMR-Guidelines-2025?bidId=
The Affordable Housing Ordinance (Below Market-Rate Housing Program) is found in San Mateo Municipal Code Section 27.16.050. This section states that specific requirements for the BMR 
Program are to be regulated via Resolution of the City Council. Resolution No. 77 (2025) provides these requirements in the form of BMR Program Guidelines. The BMR Program Guidelines 
provide (in Section IX) that preference for BMR units shall be given to persons residing or working in the City of San Mateo. This section also references any relevant policies adopted via City 
Council Resolution. Furthermore, the operative sections of Resolution No. 22 (1999) - Modified Affordable Housing Marketing Policies, state that those who live or work within the City of 
San Mateo shall be given priority over those who do not live or work in San Mateo for City-subisidized units.

City of San Mateo General Plan Progress Report 2025                                                      
 P a g e  | 2
1.
INTRODUCTION AND PURPOSE OF THIS DOCUMENT
State of California Government Code Sections 65400 and 65700 requires local planning agencies to 
provide an annual update to their legislative body, the Governor's Office of Land Use and Climate 
Innovation (LCI), previously known as the Office of Planning and Research (OPR), and the State 
Department of Housing and Community Development (HCD) on the status of the General Plan, Housing 
Element and progress in its implementation. State law requires that the General Plan Annual Progress 
Report (APR) be completed and submitted to the state by April of each year to report on 
implementation from the previous year. The General Plan APR is required even when a city may be 
undertaking a General Plan comprehensive update. 
This General Plan Progress Report looks at the City of San Mateo’s (City) progress in implementing land 
use related goals, policies and actions during the period beginning January 1, 2025, and ending on 
December 31, 2025.
2.
GENERAL PLAN BACKGROUND AND CONTENT
California law requires that every city and county adopt a long-term General Plan that addresses eight 
specific topics or “elements,” organized in any format or structure preferred by the community. The 
General Plan may also address other topics the community feels are relevant. Regardless of the format 
or issues addressed, the Plan must be internally consistent. 
The City, after a six year comprehensive effort, adopted Strive San Mateo General Plan 2040 on March 
18, 2024. Community participation played an important role in preparing the City’s General Plan 2040. 
The General Plan team held a series of meetings and events to establish the General Plan study areas; 
create the range of alternatives; confirm the draft alternatives; and receive feedback and direction on 
the preferred land use and circulation scenarios as well as on goals and policies from the community 
and, ultimately, the City Council. Additionally, other agencies and utilities were consulted including the 
Native American tribes, county agency, school districts, water districts, and regional transportation 
agencies. At the time of its adoption, San Mateo’s General Plan 2040 complied with applicable OPR 
General Plan Guidelines. 
The General Plan 2040 is organized into eight elements that meet the State requirements, as shown in 
Table 1 - General Plan Contents.

City’s Responsibility
The effectiveness of the General Plan ultimately depends on how it is implemented and maintained 
over time. State law requires that most actions of local governments affecting the physical environment 
be consistent with the General Plan. General Plan implementation is the responsibility of numerous 
departments including but not limited to City Attorney, City Manager’s Office (Economic Development), 
Community Development, Finance, Information Technology Parks and Recreation, Police, and Public 
Works.
Additionally, several other governmental agencies and utilities provide services within the City’s 
boundary. While these agencies are neither part of the City’s operational structure nor directly 
responsible for implementation of the General Plan, the City coordinates its activities with these other 
agencies and relies upon their assistance for full implementation of the General Plan. These agencies 
include but are not limited to: San Mateo Consolidated Fire Department, water districts (California 
Water Company, Estero Water District), school districts (San Mateo Foster City Unified School District, 
San Mateo High School District, California State College System), and County of San Mateo.
3.
DATE OF PRESENTATION/ACCEPTANCE BY THE LOCAL LEGISLATIVE BODY.
The General Plan Progress Report 2025 is scheduled for City Council review on March 16, 2026.
4.
DATE OF THE LAST UPDATE TO THE GENERAL PLAN.
The City Council adopted the Strive San Mate General Plan 2040 on March 18, 2024.
5.
AMENDMENTS TO THE GENERAL PLAN.
State law limits the City to amend any mandatory elements of the General Plan no more than four 
times per year. Amendments may be proposed and acted upon at any time during the year and one 
action may include multiple amendments. Any changes to the General Plan require public hearing by 
the City Council and evaluation of the environmental impacts as require by the California 
Environmental Quality Act. 
327 of 424

--- page 328 ---
City of San Mateo General Plan Progress Report 2025                                                      
 P a g e  | 4
In 2025, one General Plan Amendment was adopted for the Land Use Element. During the General Plan 
2040 adoption hearings and at a subsequent public meeting on implementation, the City Council, staff, 
and individual landowners identified 13 sites across the city where land use designations were either 
inconsistent with the existing and/or surrounding land uses, or required revisions to align with City 
Council direction on General Plan 2040.  On January 28, 2025, the Planning Commission held a public 
hearing and recommended that the City Council to adopt a resolution to amend the General Plan 2040 
Land Use Map at the 13 specified locations, which the City Council adopted on March 17, 2025.
The General Plan Land Use Map amendments are consistent with state laws relating to No Net Loss 
requirement. The No Net Loss requirement, as implemented under the Housing Crisis Act, prohibits a 
city from adopting a development policy, standard, or condition that would downzone property or 
reduce allowed residential intensity where housing is permitted. It also states that a city may only make 
such a change if it concurrently modifies standards elsewhere in the jurisdiction to ensure there is no 
net loss in residential capacity. Of the 13 sites identified, only two sites had changes to land use 
designations that would decrease the residential density. These changes shifted the designations of 
both sites to align with existing and surrounding uses and resulted in a reduction of 77 units of density 
capacity. The changes in land use designations on the remaining 11 sites, however, resulted in an 
increase of 1,751 units of density capacity. Because of the net increase of 1,674 units of capacity, the 
land use designation changes at these two locations did not affect the City’s overall residential 
development capacity pursuant to the Housing Crisis Act.
6.
HOUSING ELEMENT ANNUAL PROGRESS REPORT REQUIREMENTS. 
State law requires local agencies to complete an annual review of the implementation of the programs 
in the Housing Element toward meeting City’s Regional Housing Needs Assessment (RHNA). The City’s 
Housing Successor Agency and Housing Element Annual Progress Report are provided as separate 
attachments to the March 16, 2026, City Council report. 
7.
GENERAL PLAN COMPLIES WITH LCI’S GENERAL PLAN GUIDELINES.
San Mateo’s General Plan 2040 complies with applicable LCI’s General Plan Guidelines by incorporating 
all required topic areas, including environmental justice and identifying environmental justice or equity 
priority communities. Additionally, as stated in the background section, the City coordinated with the 
Native American Tribes, San Mateo Consolidated Fire District, water districts (California Water 
Company, Estero Water District), school districts (San Mateo Foster City Unified School District, San 
Mateo High School District, California State College System), and County of San Mateo.
8.
IMPLEMENTATION.
The Progress Report is focused on actions in the Land Use Element used to implement the General Plan. 
It also contains key milestones from other elements that will help guide land use decisions. As some of 
the General Plan actions will be implemented through the adoption of ordinances or resolutions or will 
be incorporated into the City’s regular governmental activities, they are not individually listed in the 
Progress Report, but are rather noted in Exhibit A as “continuous” along with a brief description. For 
example, this includes routine or reoccurring work in the lead department’s workload, like the City’s 
Development Review process as development proposals are reviewed for consistency with the City’s 
policies. Exhibit A is not a comprehensive list of all policies and action items in the General Plan, rather 
it summarizes the implementation status of select land use related goals, policies and actions. The 
purpose of providing Exhibit A is to streamline the review and highlight the City’s progress efficiently. 
9.
PRIORITIES FOR LAND USE DECISION MAKING ESTABLISHED BY THE LOCAL LEGISLATIVE BODY.
The following highlights major legislative actions by the City Council that support the goals of the 
General Plan:  
328 of 424

--- page 329 ---
City of San Mateo General Plan Progress Report 2025                                                      
 P a g e  | 5
Ballot Measure T (Goal LU 1, Policies H 1.20, LU 1.3 and LU 1.9) – General Plan 2040 plans for specified 
growth and change in the City primarily focused within ten study areas. Building height limits in San 
Mateo have been regulated by voter approved initiatives (Measures H, P, and Y) since 1992.  In 
November 2024, following adoption of General Plan 2040, Measure T was approved by the voters, 
which allowed for the City’s height limits to increase as outlined in the Land Use Element. Measure T 
allows the City to meet the community’s anticipated housing needs through 2040 as well as allocations 
the City will be required to plan for by the California Department of Housing and Community 
Development (HCD).  Since implementation of Measure T, planning  applications for the entitlements of 
over 5,500 residential units, with nearly 1,000 affordable units, were submitted to the City in 2025. The 
City also began working towards a Comprehensive Zoning Code Update, which will build on the 
foundation of the General Plan 2040 and Measure T.
Historic Policy Updates (Actions CD 5.8 and CD 5.9) – The City is working to update its Historic 
Preservation Ordinance (SMMC Chapter 27.66) and prepare a citywide Historic Context Statement as 
part of the implementation of San Mateo’s General Plan 2040. This effort aims to clarify criteria, 
strengthen processes, and improve transparency around historic designation and preservation. In June 
2024, the City Council held a study session to consider options for how to proceed with updating the 
City’s local historic ordinance and codes pursuant to General Plan Actions CD 5.8 and CD 5.9. In January 
2025, the City Council approved funding for the update of the City's historic policies and procedures, 
including an update to the City's Historic Preservation Ordinance and the creation of a city-wide historic 
context statement.  Rincon Consultants was selected to support City staff in working on this historic 
policy update effort. In June the City Council held a study session to receive an update on the policy 
effort and provide staff with direction ahead of community outreach and engagement.  Since the June 
City Council study session, the project team has held a number of public outreach and engagement 
activities including three focus group meetings, two virtual workshops, and three pop-up events and 
has reached over 200 community members. The City published drafts of the Historic Context Statement 
and Historic Preservation Ordinance in November and December 2025, respectively. To receive 
feedback on the drafts, the City held a virtual public workshop in mid-January 2026, followed by a City 
Council study session in late January. Additional focus groups, including with underrepresented 
community members, will be held in February and March. Following this, staff will bring a revised 
Historic Context Statement and Draft Historic Preservation Ordinance Amendments to Planning 
Commission and City Council for consideration in Spring 2026.
Code Amendments for Streamlined Review (Policy H1.6 and Action CD 7.7) – As part of the Community 
Development Department’s ongoing effort to update the Zoning Code, in 2023, the City adopted a 
Zoning Code amendment to allow residential projects with up to 25 units that meet objective design 
standards to be approved administratively. To further streamline review of development projects, on 
July 15, 2024, the City repealed and adopted new resolutions to eliminate the pre-application Planning 
Commission study session requirement, eliminate the third-party design review requirement for 
projects that meet the City’s Object Design Standards (ODS), and simplify noticing and neighborhood 
meeting procedures. The City further  amended the code  in 2025 to increase the number of housing 
units that can be approved administratively from 25 to 99 units subject to the City’s ODS. 
10. MAJOR MILESTONES AND PROJECTS.
The following section highlights major planning activities and projects that support the goals of the 
General Plan. Some of the projects are partially funded through grants, these have been identified with 
an “*”. Community planning activities/programs are multi-year initiatives and, for the purposes of the 
APR, the information below includes a status summary for projects that were initiated, continued or 
completed in 2025.

Background on Grants
Caltrans Sustainable Transportation Planning Grant– The City was awarded approximately $360,500 
from the California Department of Transportation (Caltrans) Sustainable Transportation Planning Grant 
for the development of Climate Adaptation Plan for Sea Level Rise. In September 2024, City Council 
adopted a resolution identifying approval authority incompliance with grant program requirements. 
The City began work on the plan in 2025 and will begin public outreach in the summer of 2026.  
 
Caltrans Sustainable Communities Grant – The City was awarded approximately $490,000 from the 
Caltrans Sustainable Communities grant to fund the San Mateo Complete Streets Plan and received 
notice to proceed in mid-December 2021, and initiated work on the project as described below. In 
2023, Phase 1 and 2 of outreach was completed and the City began the process of developing a 
Complete Streets North Central Plan (NCCSP). The Complete Streets Planned paused in August 
2024 due to staffing turnover and vacancies. The project is currently forecasted to restart in FY 
2026-27, once those staffing vacancies are expected to be filled.  
Community Development Block Grant (CDBG) - The City of San Mateo receives annual funding through 
the Community Development Block Grant (CDBG) from the United States Department of Housing and 
Urban Development (HUD). The CDBG program provides resources to address a wide range of 
community development needs, principally for low-income households. The Public Works Department 
utilizes a portion of the funding to deliver infrastructure improvements within the CDBG priority 
neighborhood area. In 2024 and throughout 2025, the CDBG program remained focused on intersection 
safety improvements at the Third Ave. and Norfolk St. intersection, which connects to the Third Ave. 
bicycle and pedestrian overcrossing at US 101.
Metropolitan Transportation Commission - Transit-Oriented Communities Policy Grant
In February 2025, the Metropolitan Transportation Commission (MTC) Planning Committee approved 
the City’s grant application in the amount of $610,000 to support completion of the Comprehensive 
Zoning Code Update, which will implement the Transit-Oriented Communities (TOC) policy. The TOC 
policy supports increased residential and commercial densities in areas surrounding transit stations. 
The funding will be dedicated to completing of the Comprehensive Zoning Code Update and will pay for 
City staff time to complete key tasks associated with the update and its environmental documentation.
Planning Activities  
Housing Element Update* –  Following the adoption of the Housing Element in 2024, the Housing 
Action Coalition (HAC) filed a lawsuit against the City, claiming that the Housing Element did not satisfy 
state law because sites listed on the Sites Inventory were not likely to serve as locations for future 
housing construction because of existing and active uses. In July 2025, the parties entered into a 
settlement agreement (“Settlement Agreement”). The City agreed to amend the Housing Element to 
remove certain sites from the Sites Inventory, limit the use of certain other sites for the purposes of 
“No Net Loss” calculations under Government Code Section 658631. Other updates were completed 
including adding changes related to the Measure T voter approval, revisions to the realistic capacity of 
sites based on new information, and minor changes to some of the implementation plan action items. 
The main Housing Element document and Appendix C (Housing Resources and Sites Inventory) were 
updated. All other Housing Element appendices that were adopted by the City and certified by HCD in 
July 2024 remained unchanged. On December 18, 2025, HCD determined that the City’s proposed 
Housing Element amendments are in substantial compliance with California Government Code Section 
65580 et seq. and can be certified once adopted locally. On February 23, 2026, the City Council adopted 
330 of 424

--- page 331 ---
City of San Mateo General Plan Progress Report 2025                                                      
 P a g e  | 7
Housing Element Amendments and the City is now awaiting response from HCD on their certification 
determination.
Comprehensive Zoning Code Update* - Building on the foundation of the General Plan, the Planning 
Division is working towards a comprehensive update of the City’s existing Zoning Code (Title 27). This 
will be the first comprehensive update of the City's Zoning Code in several decades.   The update will 
allow for implementation of all applicable goals and policies in the General Plan and the 2023-2031 
Housing Element (“Housing Element”), as well as address compliance with State law, meet current best 
practices and include internal consistencies for an effective Zoning Code.   In March of 2025, staff 
issued a Request for Proposals (RFP) for a qualified consultant to support the Comprehensive Zoning 
Code Update effort. On June 16, 2025, the City Council voted to appropriate funding to complete the 
Zoning Code Update and to execute a professional services agreement with PlaceWorks to support this 
effort. Following approval, PlaceWorks and City staff held a project kick-off meeting beginning of July 
2025. PlaceWorks is working closely with staff in assessing the current Zoning Code regulations. The 
final Zoning Code document will be brought before the Planning Commission for review and 
recommendation to Council for review for final adoption. Staff anticipates these final adoption hearings 
to take place during the summer of 2027.  
Minimum Residential Densities in Mixed Use Projects, Community Benefits and Density Bonus* – On 
August 19, 2024, the City held a study session with City Council to present policy options and 
recommendations on minimum residential requirements in mixed-use projects and an update to the 
existing Density Bonus/Community Benefits program and inclusionary family housing (two- and three-
bedroom affordable housing units), pursuant to Housing Element Policies H 1.5 and H 1.9. Staff is 
currently finalizing draft language to update the SMMC to include new mixed-use zone districts. The 
standards outlined within these code sections will include minimum density requirements. This 
proposed update is anticipated to go to public hearings in Spring 2026. 
The current Zoning Code does not allow for the higher-density residential and mixed-use development 
envisioned by the General Plan through the establishment of the Mixed-Use Medium II, Mixed-Use 
High, Residential Medium II and Residential High land use designations.  It was necessary to establish 
new zoning districts to allow for timely implementation of the General Plan’s adopted land use 
designations. The proposed high density zone ordinance would implement the General Plan’s land use 
framework by establishing clear and objective standards for permitted uses, development form, and 
intensity. The work on the ordinance is ongoing, and staff anticipates that this effort will move forward 
in 2026 ahead of the Comprehensive Zoning Code Update. 
ADU Ordinance Update-  Following a letter from HCD sent on October 18, 2024, staff began work to 
update the City’s Accessory Dwelling Unit (ADU) Ordinance, pursuant to Housing Element Policy H1.4, 
to address areas of the Ordinance that HCD had identified to the City as non-compliant with State ADU 
Law. As a part of this process, staff also incorporated additional updates beyond those required under 
State ADU Law to improve functionality of the Ordinance and allow for greater flexibility in the local 
ADU regulations to promote more ADU development. 
On August 26, 2025 the City held a study session with the Planning Commission to present the required 
changes and get feedback on some policy questions for additional changes proposed to local ADU 
standards. Following this study session, staff held a virtual community workshop on the ADU Ordinance 
updates on September 25, 2025. Following these outreach efforts, the draft Ordinance was further 
refined, and sent to HCD for an informal review prior to the adoption process. Staff then met with HCD 
331 of 424

--- page 332 ---
City of San Mateo General Plan Progress Report 2025                                                      
 P a g e  | 8
staff and incorporated changes based on HCD feedback into the draft ADU Ordinance for State Law 
compliance. The updated ADU Ordinance was brought to Planning Commission for a public hearing on 
December 9, 2025, followed by City Council for first reading on January 26, 2025, and was formally 
adopted by the City Council on February 2, 2026. The updated ADU Ordinance (Chapter 27.19 of the 
San Mateo Municipal Code) will become effective 30 days thereafter on March 2, 2026. The City will be 
sending the adopted ADU Ordinance to HCD for certification as required by State ADU Law, and staff 
will be working on updated supplemental materials and public outreach in partnership with the San 
Mateo County ADU Resource Center to continue to support and encourage further ADU development 
in San Mateo. 
Interim measure to address consistency between General Plan and Zoning Code for heights and 
densities - The provisions of Ordinance No. 2024-10, approved by the voters on November 5, 2024, as 
Measure T, went into effect on December 19, 2024, which allows for the full implementation of the 
Land Use Element in General Plan 2040. In the interim, in case of any conflict or inconsistency between 
Title 27 of the Municipal Code (Zoning Code) and the General Plan 2040, the uses, densities, intensities 
and heights specified in Table LU-1 (Land Use Designations) in the Land Use Element and associated 
with the Land Use Map shall control. Provision of Ordinance 2025-04 amended the municipal code to 
provide consistency between the General Plan and Zoning Code for heights and densities in the interim, 
as the City undergoes the comprehensive Zoning Code update.
Upcoming Projects  – After the passage of Measure T in 2024, the City has received planning 
applications for 19 residential development projects (six projects have submitted preliminary 
applications only) for over a total of 5,500 housing units, of which seven are mixed-use development. 
Many of these projects are utilizing State Density Bonus to increase residential units above the density 
limits under the General Plan and are also using combinations of development incentives and waivers 
under state law. Also, a majority of these projects are eligible and utilizing streamlining provisions 
under State housing laws and other provisions under the California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA) 
to accelerate the City’s review process and are subject to specific timelines such that many are likely to  
receive entitlements in 2026.  
Climate Adaptation Plan for Sea Level Rise* -  The City of San Mateo Climate Action Plan for Sea Level 
Rise will assess the vulnerability of urban development and natural ecosystems magnitude, probability, 
and severity of climate threats specific to sea level rise and will develop adaptation options to address 
those vulnerabilities. This project will produce information which will be essential to the City of San 
Mateo as it prioritizes projects which will not only safeguard the thousands of California families which 
reside within the City of San Mateo, but also the critical transportation network which serves the 
greater Bay Area region. In August 2025, City staff began work with a technical consultant to develop 
the Climate Adaptation Plan for Sea Level Rise. In November 2025, City staff coordinated with the San 
Francisco Bay Conservation and Development Commission (BCDC) to officially initiate plan 
development, a requirement of the Regional Shoreline Adaptation Plan (RSAP) Guidelines and in 
alignment with SB 272 (2023).
Climate Action Plan – The Climate Action Plan includes strategies and measures to reduce greenhouse 
gas emissions. The Climate Action Plan contains implementation measures in the following categories: 
building electrification, renewable energy, energy efficiency, municipal energy efficiency clean 
transportation fuels, sustainable transportation fuels, sustainable transportation, solid waste, water 
and wastewater, and off-road equipment. In January 2025, the City Council adopted reach codes that 
require higher energy performance standards for new construction than the state code. In July 2025, 
the City Council adopted “Electrify San Mateo: Sustainable Building Strategy,” providing a roadmap for 
332 of 424

--- page 333 ---
City of San Mateo General Plan Progress Report 2025                                                      
 P a g e  | 9
future decarbonization policies in San Mateo. Additionally, staff continue to work on electric vehicle 
charging infrastructure to support the City’s transition to a green fleet.
Complete Streets Plan* - The Complete Streets Plan will complement the City’s General Plan Update by 
creating an actionable plan rooted in safety for all modes and will result in policies, goals, and 
prioritized projects that are focused on improving mobility, equity, connectivity, and sustainability to 
build a better circulation network for the City’s future. The Plan will provide the basis for projects that 
are planned, designed, constructed, and maintained for all roadway users, allowing the City to develop 
a safe mobility network for many years to come. In 2023, City staff and the consultant team completed 
Phases I and II of the community engagement plan and began the process of developing a Complete 
Streets North Central Plan (NCCSP). Work continued on both plans through 2024, with 80% of the 
Complete Streets Plan and 85% of the NCCSP completed by the end of the year. It should be noted that 
through the Plan, the City may also qualify for future grant opportunities to implement Plan programs 
and capital improvement projects. The Complete Streets Planned paused in August 2024 due to staffing 
turnover and vacancies. The project is currently forecasted to restart in FY 2026-27, once those staffing 
vacancies are expected to be filled. 
Major Construction/Development Projects
Planning applications that were submitted during one reporting year typically receive their entitlements 
in the next reporting year. Consistent with the General Plan APR reporting requirements, planning 
application entitlements that were approved during the reporting year are included in the APR report. 
During 2025, the City approved entitlements for 24 residential units, but none were for larger 
development projects. The City also made progress on several publicly funded projects. Major 
residential projects for which building permits have been issued and other publicly funded projects are 
highlighted below with a brief status update:
Bay Meadows Phase II MU2 and MU3 – Building permits for Mixed Use Blocks 2 and 3 with a combined 
303,000 square-feet of office uses and 67 housing units, were issued in November 2025, but 
construction has not begun yet.
477 9th Avenue – On February 20, 2024, the City Council approved the mixed-use development 
consisting of offices and 120 residential units. Building permit applications were submitted in 2024, 
issued in 2025, and it is now under construction. It is anticipated to be completed by January 2027.
3rd Ave. and Norfolk St. Intersection Safety Improvements* - A public survey was conducted in 
September of 2023 to understand how the public currently utilizes the intersection of 3rd Ave. and 
Norfolk St. and to identify potential areas of concern. The results of the survey were then used to guide 
the creation of the Intersection Improvement Concept Plan, which was released to the public on 
September 25, 2024. Project design was finalized by the end of 2024. The improvements will modify the 
intersection of 3rd Ave. and Norfolk St. to improve pedestrian and bicycle safety, especially for people 
using the 3rd Ave. overcrossing of Highway 101. The project will also improve the bicycle connection 
between the intersection of 3rd Ave. and Norfolk St. and the San Mateo Creek bicycle path. A large 
element of the improvements include modifications to the traffic signal timing and operation to provide 
additional pedestrian and cyclist safety while not significantly impacting major vehicle movements and 
delay through the area. Construction on the improvements began in February 2025. Construction 
continued through 2025 with completion of the new bike path on Norfolk, construction of underground 
systems (new storm drain, electrical conduit and signal pole foundations), and installation of new signal 
poles and hardware. Construction is now nearly complete and the new traffic signal timing and 
333 of 424

10
operation, including the new signalized bicycle crossing at San Mateo Creek, is anticipated to be 
implemented late February/early March 2026.
1530 Susan Ct. Capital Improvement Project - The Marina Branch Public Library is undergoing 
restoration which includes essential improvements to ensure the safety and longevity of the facility. 
Planned improvements include:
 
•
Foundation & structural repairs 
•

•

•

•
Newly updated interior

Relocated deck

the Project contractor completed site demolition and selective interior demolition. Foundation work is 
currently in progress.
435 E. 3rd - On February 14, 2023, the Planning Commission approved the mixed-use development 
consisting of offices and 5 residential units. On May 15, 2025, the Zoning Administrator approved a 
Minor Modification to the Conditions of Approval, allowing the merger of the two existing lots. 
Additionally, a two-year extension was granted, extending its expiration date to February 14, 2027. 
A demolition permit was issued for the site on December 23, 2025, followed by issuance of the 
superstructure permit in February 2026. As of February 2026, demolition is substantially complete, and 
the site is nearly prepared for foundation construction. Project completion is anticipated in the second 
quarter of 2027.

Action LU 10.9 Resilience of Critical Facilities and Public 
Infrastructure. Identify critical facilities and public infrastructure in 
areas vulnerable to climate change hazards, and work to site, 
design, and upgrade these facilities with consideration for future 
increases in severity that may occur over the anticipated life of 
the development. In cases where facilities cannot be sustainably 
maintained, evaluate the costs and benefits of relocation. Where 
facilities can be safely sited for the near term, but future impacts 
are likely, prepare an adaptive management plan detailing steps 
for maintenance, retrofitting, and/or relocation.

Prasanna W. Rasiah, City Attorney
PREPARED BY:
City Attorney's Office
MEETING DATE:
March 16, 2026 
SUBJECT:
Charter Amendments — Study Session
RECOMMENDATION:
Hold a study session regarding proposed amendments to the City Charter to reflect the change to district elections, 
address other outdated provisions, and provide direction to staff.
BACKGROUND:
During the “Blue Sky” Goal Setting Workshop on February 7, 2026, the City Council chose to include City Charter 
amendments as a priority for FY 2026/27. As directed by the Council, the amendments are to address non-controversial 
matters, such as reflecting the change to district elections, in an effort to “clean up” outdated provisions in the Charter.  
Each of these changes are addressed later in this report and are mostly the same as changes proposed in 2024 during a 
separate Charter review process, which was ultimately put on hold.  
DISCUSSION:
District Elections
Existing Charter Language (Sec. 2.01(a))
Proposed Charter Language
There shall be a city council of five members elected by 
the voters of the city at large.  
There shall be a city council of five members elected by 
the voters of the city at large by districts.  Any recall 
election or special election or appointment to fill a 
vacancy shall also be by district.  
Following each decennial federal census, and at other 
such times as provided by law, the city council shall, 
by resolution or ordinance, adopt boundaries for all 
council districts so that all of the districts shall comply 
with state and federal law.  The term of office of any 
councilmember who has been elected and whose 
term of office has not expired shall not be affected by 
any change in the boundaries of the district from 
which the councilmember was elected.
The members of the Council are of course now elected by district rather than at large, following a 2021 demand letter 
375 of 424

--- page 376 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
claiming a violation of the California Voting Rights Act and demanding a change in City electoral practices. The district 
election process is also codified in the San Mateo Municipal Code. The additional proposed language clarifies that a 
redistricting process will occur every ten years, consistent with state and federal law, and that an appointee to fill a 
vacancy must live in the same district as the Councilmember who vacated the seat at issue.  Additionally, where the 
boundaries of a district are changed, the proposed language clarifies that the terms of then current Councilmembers will 
not be affected.  
Councilmembers Elected in 2017
Existing Charter Language (Sec. 2.01(d).)
Proposed Charter Language
Provisions applicable to the councilmembers 
elected at the general municipal election held in 
2015 and the councilmembers elected at the 
general municipal election held in 2017.
1.
The incumbent councilmembers elected at 
the general municipal election held in 2015 
shall have their term extended by one year, 
until the general municipal election held in 
2020.
2.
The three councilmembers elected at the 
general municipal election held in 2017 shall 
hold office for a term of five years, 
commencing on the first regular council 
meeting in December 2017 until the general 
municipal election held in 2022.
3.
These provisions are necessary to effectuate 
the change in timing of general municipal 
elections from odd-numbered years to even-
numbered years, as approved by the voters 
of city in the general municipal election held 
in 2017.  
Reserved. Provisions applicable to the 
councilmembers elected at the general municipal 
election held in 2015 and the councilmembers 
elected at the general municipal election held in 
2017.
1.
The incumbent councilmembers elected at 
the general municipal election held in 2015 
shall have their term extended by one year, 
until the general municipal election held in 
2020.
2.
The three councilmembers elected at the 
general municipal election held in 2017 shall 
hold office for a term of five years, 
commencing on the first regular council 
meeting in December 2017 until the general 
municipal election held in 2022.
3.
These provisions are necessary to effectuate 
the change in timing of general municipal 
elections from odd-numbered years to even-
numbered years, as approved by the voters 
of city in the general municipal election held 
in 2017.
This Charter provision was added by the voters in 2017 in order to comply with Senate Bill 415 (SB 415) (2015). SB 415 
required cities to realign their elections to even numbered years if prior odd-year elections had resulted in a significant 
decrease in voter turnout. The City’s 2017 ballot measure did so, also extending the terms of Council members elected in 
2015 and 2017 by one year to facilitate this goal. It passed by a vote of 81.4% to 18.6%. However, the terms of office for 
Council members elected in 2015 and 2017 have now ended (as of 2022 for the latter), and this language is no longer 
needed. Charter Section 2.01(c) provides for the staggered election of Councilmembers in 2020 (two seats) and 2022 
(three seats), and even-numbered years thereafter, for a term of four years.
376 of 424

--- page 377 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
Forfeiture of Office for Absence from the City
Existing Charter Language (Sec. 2.07)
Proposed Charter Language
 
Any councilmember shall forfeit his/her office who (1) fails 
to qualify within 10 days after appointment or certification 
of election, or (2) is absent from the city continuously for 
more than 30 days without permission of a majority of the 
remaining councilmembers, or (3) fails to attend three 
consecutive regular meetings of the council without being 
excused by a majority of the remaining councilmembers, 
and the excuse entered in the minutes, or (4) fails to 
attend at least two-thirds of all regular meetings of the 
council during any 12-month period, or (5) is convicted of 
a violation of any express provision of this Charter or of a 
crime involving moral turpitude, or (6) attempts to 
influence the city manager or city attorney in the making 
of any appointment or in the purchase of supplies, or (7) 
lacks at any time during his/her term of office any 
qualification for the office prescribed by this Charter or by 
law.
 
Any councilmember shall forfeit his/her office who (1) fails 
to qualify within 10 days after appointment or certification 
of election, or (2) is absent from the city continuously for 
more than 30 60 days without permission of a majority of 
the remaining councilmembers, or (3) fails to attend three 
consecutive regular meetings of the council without being 
excused by a majority of the remaining councilmembers, 
and the excuse entered in the minutes, or (4) fails to 
attend at least two-thirds of all regular meetings of the 
council during any 12-month period, or (5) is convicted of 
a violation of any express provision of this Charter or of a 
crime involving moral turpitude, or (6) attempts to 
influence the city manager or city attorney in the making 
of any appointment or in the purchase of supplies, or (7) 
lacks at any time during his/her term of office any 
qualification for the office prescribed by this Charter or by 
law.
This proposed change would align the Charter with state law applicable to general law cities, specifically Government Code 
section 36513.  That statute provides for a vacancy where a Councilmember is absent without permission from regular 
Council meetings for 60 days consecutively from the last regular meeting they attended.  This revision would also offer 
more flexibility for Councilmembers who may be out of town for extended periods for personal or work-related reasons.   
Time to Fill Council Vacancies
Existing Charter Language (Sec. 2.08)
Proposed Charter Language
 
A vacancy on the city council from whatever cause arising 
shall be filled by appointment by the council provided, 
that if the council fails to agree or for any other reason 
does not fill such vacancy within 30 days after the same 
occurs, then such vacancy shall be filled by the mayor. The 
appointee shall hold office until the next general election, 
when a successor shall be chosen by the electors for the 
unexpired term. If for any reason the seats of a majority of 
the council become vacant, then the city clerk shall call a 
special election at once to fill the vacancies for the 
unexpired terms, and the same shall be conducted 
substantially in the manner provided for general municipal 
elections. The candidates receiving the most votes shall 
serve the longer, if any, of the unexpired terms, and in 
case of ties the terms shall be fixed by lot.  
 
 
A vacancy on the city council from whatever cause arising 
shall be filled by appointment by the council provided, 
that if the council fails to agree or for any other reason 
does not fill such vacancy within 30 60 days after the same 
occurs, then such vacancy shall be filled by the mayor. The

The time for the Council to decide on filling a vacancy would be increased from 30 to 60 days. This is important because if 
a vacancy occurs due to a Councilmember being elected to another office, that will likely occur in November. The existing 
377 of 424

--- page 378 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
30-day period would then expire in December during the holiday season. Extending the period to 60 days would allow for 
increased outreach to the community and a more deliberate application, interview, and selection process. 
 
The draft language also eliminates text allowing candidates receiving the most votes to serve the longer of unexpired 
terms (and addressing tie votes) where a majority of the Council seats become vacant.  Following the shift to district 
elections, candidates would no longer run for one of several at-large seats and would instead run for a single seat in their 
district.  Thus, the current language is no longer necessary.

The proposed language would remove 6:30 p.m. as the start time for Council meetings and simply allow the time to be 
determined by resolution, which will provide the Council with more flexibility.

Any ordinance declared by the council to be

--- page 379 ---

day following the date on which it was adopted, but

except one for emergency appropriations or calling

The draft language would allow for the publication of a summary of an emergency ordinance (more commonly known as
an urgency ordinance). Currently, the Charter does not allow publication of a summary, and therefore the entire urgency 
ordinance must be published in the newspaper. This change would result in modest cost savings, but more importantly 
would allow for the same flexibility in publishing urgency ordinances that exists for standard ordinances under Charter 
Section 2.15(d).
Furthermore, this proposal would eliminate language requiring the automatic repeal of urgency ordinances on the 91st day
after adoption. This language was not part of the original 1922 Charter and was added in 1970. The circumstances
requiring the urgency ordinance would not necessarily have been resolved approximately three months after adoption.
Eliminating this text would not prevent the Council from affirmatively repealing an urgency ordinance as appropriate.

The language proposed for elimination originally appeared in the 1922 Charter and has only undergone minor changes 
over the years.  As the Council is well aware, the manner in which election campaigns are conducted has vastly changed 
over the last century.  Instead of a statement with the prescribed information constituting a significant source of 
information for the voters, other sources of information are much more commonly used during an election campaign, such 
as Internet websites with written material and videos, and social media.  Candidates may also submit a statement to be 
included in a voter information guide that is distributed to voters.  This existing provision is thus outdated and is 
appropriate for removal.

Selection of Newspaper – Publication of Notices
Existing Charter Language (Sec. 9.07)
Proposed Charter Language
The council periodically shall advertise for or call for the 
submission of sealed proposals or bids from all 
newspapers adjudicated to be newspapers of general 
circulation within the city, or if none, then from 
newspapers adjudicated to be newspapers of general 
circulation with in the County of San Mateo, for the 
publication of all ordinances and other legal notices 
required to be published. The council may designate the 
requirements for award of contract. The contract therefor 
shall be awarded to the lowest responsible bidder, 
provided the rates for such publication shall not exceed 
the customary rate charged for publishing legal notices of 
a private character. The newspaper to whom such contract 
is awarded shall be known and designated as the official 
city newspaper.
In the event no such newspaper will contract with the city 
as herein provided, or if the official city newspaper is not 
published, then notice of the matters required to be 
published in the official city newspaper shall be given by 
posting copies thereof at three or more public places in 
the city as designated by the council, and such posting 
shall be equivalent to legal publication.
 
The council periodically shall issue a request for proposals 
advertise for or call for the submission of sealed proposals 
or bids from all newspapers adjudicated to be newspapers 
of general circulation within the city, or if none, then from 
newspapers adjudicated to be newspapers of general 
circulation within with in the County of San Mateo, for the 
publication of all ordinances and other legal notices 
required to be published. The council may designate the 
requirements for award of contract. The contract therefor 
shall be awarded to the lowest responsible bidder whose 
proposal is the most advantageous to the city, 
considering price and other appropriate factors, provided 
the rates for such publication shall not exceed the 
customary rate charged for publishing legal notices of a 
private character. The newspaper to whom such contract 
is awarded shall be known and designated as the official 
city newspaper.
In the event no such newspaper will contract with the city 
as herein provided, or if the official city newspaper is not 
published, then notice of the matters required to be 
published in the official city newspaper shall be given by 
posting copies thereof at three or more public places in 
the city as designated by the council, and such posting 
shall be equivalent to legal publication.
The proposed revisions are designed to provide more flexibility in selecting an official newspaper in which public hearing 
notices and other announcements are required to be published.  The current wording is narrowly focused on the lowest 
bidder, while the proposed language would more readily allow consideration of other factors such as circulation within the 
city and frequency of publication, in addition to price.  These revisions would allow the City to help ensure that the 
newspaper designated to publish official notices is more likely to reach San Mateo residents.  Finally, it corrects a typo 
where “within” was inadvertently separated into two words.  Also note that calling for a selection process “periodically” 
provides flexibility and is not proposed to be changed, but doing so approximately every five years is appropriate.   
Miscellaneous Charter Revisions
Staff also plans to propose miscellaneous “clean-up” revisions to the Charter, namely adding gender neutral language 
where needed.    
CHARTER AMENDMENT PROCESS
Under state law, the City Council may propose a charter amendment and submit it to the voters at the next statewide 
general election, at least 88 days before the election. Govt. §34458(a). The charter amendment will not be adopted until
it is approved by a majority vote.  Before approving the submittal of a charter amendment to the voters, the City Council 
must hold at least two public hearings, with published and posted notice, at least 21 calendar days prior to the date of 
each public hearing. Govt. §34458(b).  The second public hearing must be held at least 30 days after the first public 
381 of 424

--- page 382 ---
CITY OF SAN MATEO
hearing, and at least one of the two hearings must be held outside of normal business hours to facilitate public 
participation. Govt. §34458(b). In this case, both public hearings will take place in the evening during a regular Council 
meeting.  The Council cannot vote on whether to approve submitting the proposal to the voters until 21 days after the 
second public hearing. Govt. §34458(b). Also, while a public hearing notice is not legally required for the Council action to 
place a measure on the ballot, staff has built such a notice into the process below for increased transparency.  
The Charter amendment must also be filed with the California Secretary of State and the County Recorder, and must be 
published in the official state statutes. Govt. §§34459 - 34461. 
Below is the schedule that builds in a buffer between the projected date of submittal to the voters and the statutory 
deadline of 88 days before the election. This will allow for better coordination with the County Elections office and an 
additional Council meeting, if necessary.

BUDGET IMPACT:
There is no budget impact associated with this study session. Should the Council direct staff to pursue further action on 
charter amendments, further analysis and scoping will be required. Hiring a ballot measure consultant and polling 
consultant will result in additional costs. Also note that consistent with state law, no public funds can be used to advocate 
for or against a ballot measure. Instead, these funds would be used for polling and education and information to 
determine how each measure should be formulated. Finally, placing the measure on the ballot at the consolidated 
November 3, 2026 election will also cost approximately $20,400, which represents the incremental additional cost of 
including a second measure on the ballot on top of a potential local revenue measure.  But this merely represents a rough 
early estimate and is subject to change.

result in direct or indirect physical changes in the environment. (CEQA Guidelines Section 15378(b)(5).)
